- Step 4: nŠļŅu kh√īng match, kiŠĽÉm tra 5 gate trong `build_lswitch_arp_nd_responder_known_ips`: LSP kh√īng phŠļ£i `external`, kh√īng c√≥ `disable_arp_nd_rsp=true`, addresses kh√īng phŠļ£i `unknown`, etc.
- Step 5: `tcpdump -i geneve_sys_6081 arp` cross-check c√≥ bao nhi√™u ARP ńĎi qua tunnel

Cross-link PhŠļßn 18.0 ¬ßARP responder + BUM suppression, PhŠļßn 13.18 ¬ßls_in_arp_rsp.

**Li√™n quan mŠļ≠t thiŠļŅt.** Tightly coupled: `Logical_Switch_Port.addresses` (nguŠĽďn known IP), `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` (alternative source), `Logical_Switch_Port.options:disable_arp_nd_rsp` (per-LSP toggle), `LS_IN_L2_LKUP` (downstream consumer khi kh√īng match priority 50, fallback flood), `MC_FLOOD` multicast group (broadcast destination khi kh√īng suppress), action `nd_na`. Loose: `Logical_Router_Port.peer` (cho LR-LS interconnect, LRP c√≥ ARP responder ri√™ng ŠĽü LR_IN_IP_INPUT), Geneve tunnel (load giŠļ£m khi suppression hoŠļ°t ńĎŠĽông).

**Kh√°c biŠĽát giŠĽĮa c√°c phi√™n bŠļ£n.**
- OVN 2.5 (2016): introduce stage cho IPv4 ARP responder
- OVN 2.7: th√™m IPv6 Neighbor Solicitation responder (c√Ļng stage), ńĎŠĽēi t√™n th√†nh ARP_ND_RSP
- OVN 21.06: tŠĽĎi ∆įu compile, group flow theo (MAC, IP[]) thay v√¨ per-IP
- OVN 22.03 (baseline): stable, hŠĽó trŠĽ£ `disable_arp_nd_rsp` per-LSP option
- OVN 22.06: th√™m stage `LS_IN_PRE_ARP_ND_RSP` (stage 17) l√†m pre-processing hint
- OVN 24.03: tŠĽĎi ∆įu memory cho LS c√≥ >1000 LSP

**C√°ch quan s√°t + x√°c minh.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep -A2 "ls_in_arp_rsp"
  table=18 (ls_in_arp_rsp), priority=50,
    match=(arp.tpa == 10.0.0.5 && arp.op == 1),
    action=(eth.dst = eth.src; eth.src = aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01; arp.op = 2;
            arp.tha = arp.sha; arp.sha = aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01;
            arp.tpa = arp.spa; arp.spa = 10.0.0.5;
            outport = inport; flags.loopback = 1; output;)
  table=18 (ls_in_arp_rsp), priority=0,
    match=(1), action=(next;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=26 | head -2
  cookie=0x1, table=26, n_packets=42, arp,arp_tpa=10.0.0.5,arp_op=1,
    actions=move:NXM_OF_ETH_SRC[]->NXM_OF_ETH_DST[],
            mod_dl_src:aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01,load:0x2->NXM_OF_ARP_OP[],...

$ # Verify suppression: tr√™n chassis target, KH√ĒNG thŠļ•y ARP request ńĎi qua tunnel
$ tcpdump -i any -nn 'udp port 6081 and arp' 2>/dev/null
  (no output expected khi suppression hoŠļ°t ńĎŠĽông)
```

**Source code tham chiŠļŅu.**
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lswitch_arp_nd_responder_known_ips()`: h√†m ch√≠nh sinh flow priority 50 (verified branch-22.03)
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lswitch_arp_nd_responder_default()`: priority 0 fallback
- `lib/actions.c` parser `nd_na` action
- `controller/lflow.c` dŠĽčch action ARP/ND build xuŠĽĎng OVS sequence
- `lib/lflow.h` macro `S_SWITCH_IN_ARP_ND_RSP = 18` (branch-22.03)
- `northd/ovn-northd.8.xml` ¬ß"Ingress Table 18: ARP/ND responder" doc
- Pre-existing reference: PhŠļßn 18.0 ¬ß3 (5 gate ńĎiŠĽĀu kiŠĽán northd), PhŠļßn 13.16 d√≤ng 169

**Tr∆įŠĽĚng hŠĽ£p sŠĽĪ cŠĽĎ thŠĽĪc tŠļŅ.** Q4/2024 production OpenStack-OVN cluster 800 hypervisor: monitoring b√°o Geneve tunnel CPU usage tńÉng tŠĽę ~5% l√™n 35% sau khi th√™m 1 tenant network mŠĽõi vŠĽõi 200 VNF. Investigation: `tcpdump -i geneve_sys_6081 arp | head -100` thŠļ•y mŠĽói gi√Ęy ~5000 ARP request ńĎi qua tunnel mesh (kŠĽ≥ vŠĽćng <100). `ovn-sbctl lflow-list <vnf-network> | grep "ls_in_arp_rsp" | wc -l` chŠĽČ trŠļ£ vŠĽĀ 1 flow priority 0 (default), kh√īng c√≥ priority 50. Root cause: tenant deploy VNF vŠĽõi `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vnf-N "<MAC> unknown"` (v√¨ VNF c√≥ nhiŠĽĀu IP ńĎŠĽông ph√≠a sau, kh√īng declare cŠĽĎ ńĎŠĽčnh). 200 LSP `addresses=unknown` khiŠļŅn northd kh√īng sinh ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c priority 50 ‚Üí mŠĽći ARP cho IP trong tenant n√†y phŠļ£i flood. Fix: t√°ch traffic management network khŠĽŹi data plane VNF, tenant declare cŠĽĎ ńĎŠĽčnh MAC + IP cho management interface (1 IP per VNF), giŠĽĮ `unknown` chŠĽČ cho data interface. Sau fix, tunnel CPU drop vŠĽĀ 7%. Cross-link PhŠļßn 18.0 ¬ßaddresses=unknown anti-pattern.

**B√†i tŠļ≠p synthetic.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-arpnd
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-arpnd lsp-A
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-A "aa:11:11:11:11:11 10.0.0.5"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-arpnd lsp-B
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-B "aa:22:22:22:22:22 10.0.0.6"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-arpnd lsp-VNF
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-VNF "aa:33:33:33:33:33 unknown"
# Lab task 1: ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-arpnd | grep ls_in_arp_rsp ‚Üí ńĎŠļŅm priority 50 (kŠĽ≥ vŠĽćng 2 cho A + B)
# Lab task 2: ovn-trace ls-arpnd 'inport=="lsp-A" && arp.op==1 && arp.tpa==10.0.0.6' ‚Üí match priority 50
# Lab task 3: ovn-trace ls-arpnd 'inport=="lsp-A" && arp.op==1 && arp.tpa==10.0.0.99' ‚Üí fall priority 0 (unknown IP)
# Lab task 4: ovn-nbctl lsp-set-options lsp-B disable_arp_nd_rsp=true ‚Üí flow priority 50 cho 10.0.0.6 biŠļŅn mŠļ•t
# Lab task 5: gŠĽ≠i NS IPv6: ovn-trace ls-arpnd 'nd_ns && nd.target==<ipv6 known>' ‚Üí match nd_na reply
```

**LŠĽói th∆įŠĽĚng gŠļ∑p + t√≠n hiŠĽáu chŠļ©n ńĎo√°n.**
- Mode A "kh√īng c√≥ flow priority 50": LSP `addresses=unknown` hoŠļ∑c `disable_arp_nd_rsp=true` ‚Üí declare IP cŠĽĎ ńĎŠĽčnh hoŠļ∑c bŠļ≠t lŠļ°i
- Mode B "ARP storm d√Ļ responder bŠļ≠t": c√≥ nhiŠĽĀu LSP `addresses=unknown` chiŠļŅm tŠĽ∑ lŠĽá lŠĽõn ‚Üí audit `ovn-nbctl --columns=name,addresses list lsp` count unknown
- Mode C "responder reply sai MAC": c√≥ 2 LSP c√Ļng IP do typo ‚Üí northd compile last-write-wins ‚Üí grep IP duplicate trong NBDB
- Mode D "IPv6 ND kh√īng reply": LSP thiŠļŅu IPv6 link-local trong addresses ‚Üí th√™m `fe80::aabb:ccff:fedd:eeff` v√†o addresses

**So s√°nh vŠĽõi hŠĽá kh√°c.** Linux bridge `l2population` plugin (ML2/OVS): t∆į∆°ng tŠĽĪ vŠĽĀ function (suppress ARP broadcast bŠļĪng pre-distributed FDB) nh∆įng dŠĽĪa tr√™n agent + RPC, kh√īng inline pipeline. EVPN Type-2 route + ARP suppression (FRR/Cisco): pre-distribute MAC/IP qua BGP, suppress local; OVN l√†m t∆į∆°ng ńĎ∆į∆°ng nh∆įng qua NBDB sync thay v√¨ BGP. Cisco ACI `endpoint learning` + ARP optimization analog. NSX-T ARP suppression (c√Ļng pattern: controller pre-knows MAC/IP, distribute responder rule xuŠĽĎng host) gŠļßn nhŠļ•t vŠĽõi OVN. AWS VPC: managed, kh√īng expose pipeline; ARP cho ENI ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c resolve qua VPC API ngŠļßm.

---

## ¬ß13.19.22 LS_IN_DHCP_RESPONSE ‚ÄĒ emit DHCPOFFER/ACK reply sau khi DHCP_OPTIONS build payload

**Kh√°i niŠĽám.** `LS_IN_DHCP_RESPONSE` l√† stage logic ingress LS ńĎŠĽ©ng ngay sau `LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS` (¬ß13.19.5), ńĎŠļ£m nhiŠĽám b∆įŠĽõc **emit reply DHCP** ra ngo√†i. Sau khi stage tr∆įŠĽõc gŠĽći `put_dhcp_opts` build xong DHCPOFFER/DHCPACK payload v√† set `REGBIT_DHCP_OPTS_RESULT` (`reg0[3]`), stage n√†y d√Ļng kŠļŅt quŠļ£ ńĎ√≥ ńĎŠĽÉ tŠļ°o packet phŠļ£n hŠĽďi: swap eth.src ‚áĄ eth.dst, ip4.src ‚áĄ ip4.dst, ńĎŠļ∑t udp.src=67/udp.dst=68, set `outport = inport; flags.loopback = 1; output;`. LoŠļ°i: **pipeline DHCP reply emitter**, sub-loŠļ°i "stateful response after option build".

**LŠĽčch sŠĽ≠ + bŠĽĎi cŠļ£nh.** Stage t√°ch ra c√Ļng `LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS` tŠĽę OVN 2.6 (2016) khi Pfaff + Reddy refactor inline DHCP server. Tr∆įŠĽõc OVN 2.6, mŠĽôt stage duy nhŠļ•t xŠĽ≠ l√Ĺ cŠļ£ option build lŠļęn reply emit, dŠļęn ńĎŠļŅn Logical_Flow phŠĽ©c tŠļ°p kh√≥ debug. T√°ch 2 stage gi√ļp: (a) stage OPTIONS focus build payload + set kŠļŅt quŠļ£ v√†o REGBIT, (b) stage RESPONSE chŠĽČ check REGBIT rŠĽďi emit. OVN 2.8 (2017) mŠĽü rŠĽông pattern cho DHCPv6 (c√Ļng cŠļ∑p DHCPV6_OPTIONS / DHCPV6_RESPONSE). OVN 22.03 ŠĽēn ńĎŠĽčnh, OVN 24.03 tŠĽĎi ∆įu compile cho high-density tenant.

**VŠĽč tr√≠ trong kiŠļŅn tr√ļc.** Stage logic 20 trong LS_IN pipeline, √°nh xŠļ° OF table 28 tr√™n br-int (theo 13.16 d√≤ng 171). ńźŠĽ©ng ngay sau `LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS` (stage 19, OF table 27) v√† tr∆įŠĽõc `LS_IN_DNS_LOOKUP` (stage 21). Scope: per-packet (chŠĽČ DHCP UDP port 67/68), per-LSP (mŠĽói LSP c√≥ flow ri√™ng ŠĽ©ng vŠĽõi DHCP_Options gŠļĮn v√†o). Stage chŠļ°y local tr√™n chassis cŠĽßa VM gŠĽ≠i DHCPDISCOVER/REQUEST.

**Vai tr√≤.** Vai tr√≤ ch√≠nh: **emit packet DHCPOFFER/DHCPACK** quay ng∆įŠĽ£c vŠĽĀ client sau khi stage tr∆įŠĽõc build payload th√†nh c√īng. Vai tr√≤ phŠĽ•: drop packet nŠļŅu stage tr∆įŠĽõc fail (`reg0[3] == 0`, v√≠ dŠĽ• offerip ngo√†i subnet) ‚ÄĒ kh√īng emit reply lŠĽói tr√°nh confuse client. PhŠļ°m vi vai tr√≤: chŠĽČ emit cho DHCP success path; failure path ‚Üí drop. Stage n√†y kh√īng build payload, chŠĽČ thao t√°c header L2/L3/L4 + output.

**V√¨ sao sinh ra.** Pre-existence pain (tr∆įŠĽõc OVN 2.6 split): stage DHCP duy nhŠļ•t chŠĽ©a cŠļ£ "if put_dhcp_opts th√†nh c√īng th√¨ swap MAC/IP rŠĽďi output, ng∆įŠĽ£c lŠļ°i drop". Logical_Flow n√†y d√†i v√† phŠĽ©c tŠļ°p, kh√≥ test ri√™ng phŠļßn build vs phŠļßn emit. Khi user b√°o "DHCPOFFER kh√īng vŠĽĀ client", kh√≥ x√°c ńĎŠĽčnh lŠĽói ŠĽü build (option sai) hay ŠĽü emit (swap MAC nhŠļßm). T√°ch 2 stage cho ph√©p isolated test: stage 19 test build payload ńĎŠĽôc lŠļ≠p, stage 20 test emit logic. CŇ©ng gi√ļp pattern reuse: nŠļŅu sau n√†y th√™m DHCPv6 hoŠļ∑c protocol kh√°c, chŠĽČ th√™m cŠļ∑p OPTIONS/RESPONSE mŠĽõi.

**VŠļ•n ńĎŠĽĀ giŠļ£i quyŠļŅt.** CŠĽ• thŠĽÉ: (a) sau khi `put_dhcp_opts` th√†nh c√īng ŠĽü stage 19, packet vŠļęn c√≤n header gŠĽĎc cŠĽßa DHCPDISCOVER (src=0.0.0.0, dst=255.255.255.255, src MAC = client MAC), (b) cŠļßn reverse h∆įŠĽõng ńĎŠĽÉ packet trŠĽü th√†nh DHCPOFFER hŠĽ£p lŠĽá vŠĽĀ client. C√°ch giŠļ£i: priority 100 flow `match=(reg0[3] == 1 && eth.dst == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && udp.src == 68 && udp.dst == 67)` action `eth.dst = eth.src; eth.src = aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01; ip4.src = 10.0.0.1 /* server_id */; ip4.dst = 255.255.255.255; udp.src = 67; udp.dst = 68; outport = inport; flags.loopback = 1; output;`. Priority 0 default `next` cho non-DHCP packet. PhŠļ°m vi giŠļ£i quyŠļŅt: chŠĽČ DHCPv4 success path; DHCPv6 ŠĽü stage t∆į∆°ng ńĎ∆į∆°ng `LS_IN_DHCPV6_RESPONSE`.

**TŠļßm quan trŠĽćng.** MŠĽ©c trung b√¨nh. PhŠĽ• thuŠĽôc v√†o stage `LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS` (stage 19) ‚ÄĒ nŠļŅu stage 19 fail (REGBIT 0), stage 20 kh√īng emit. CŠļ£ 2 stage phŠļ£i hoŠļ°t ńĎŠĽông ńĎŠĽďng bŠĽô th√¨ VM mŠĽõi nhŠļ≠n IP. Engineer must-know: hiŠĽÉu cŠļ∑p OPTIONS/RESPONSE l√† pattern check-then-emit vŠĽõi REGBIT l√†m cŠļßu nŠĽĎi; biŠļŅt check `reg0[3]` khi debug ńĎŠĽÉ x√°c ńĎŠĽčnh stage n√†o fail.

**C∆° chŠļŅ hoŠļ°t ńĎŠĽông.** H√†m sinh flow: c√Ļng `build_lswitch_dhcp_options_and_response()` trong `northd/northd.c` vŠĽõi stage 19 (verified branch-22.03). H√†m sinh 1 flow stage 20 cho mŠĽói LSP c√≥ dhcpv4_options gŠļĮn:

```
table=20 (ls_in_dhcp_response), priority=100,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
         ip4.src == 0.0.0.0 && ip4.dst == 255.255.255.255 &&
         udp.src == 68 && udp.dst == 67 && reg0[3] == 1),
  action=(eth.dst = eth.src;
          eth.src = aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01;
          ip4.src = 10.0.0.1; /* server_id */
          ip4.dst = 255.255.255.255;
          udp.src = 67;
          udp.dst = 68;
          outport = inport;
          flags.loopback = 1;
          output;)

table=20 (ls_in_dhcp_response), priority=0,
  match=(1), action=(next;)
```

L∆įu √Ĺ: `reg0[3] == 1` (REGBIT_DHCP_OPTS_RESULT) l√† ńĎiŠĽĀu kiŠĽán match cŠĽĎt l√Ķi ‚ÄĒ n√≥ ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c set trong stage 19 nŠļŅu `put_dhcp_opts` th√†nh c√īng. NŠļŅu stage 19 fail (offerip ngo√†i subnet, missing required option), `reg0[3]=0`, packet r∆°i xuŠĽĎng priority 0 next ŠĽü stage 20, eventually drop hoŠļ∑c broadcast (trong cŠļ£ 2 tr∆įŠĽĚng hŠĽ£p client kh√īng nhŠļ≠n reply). Action `flags.loopback = 1` cŠļßn thiŠļŅt v√¨ `outport = inport` (packet quay vŠĽĀ c√Ļng port).

**C√°ch kŠĽĻ s∆į vŠļ≠n h√†nh th√†nh thŠļ°o.** (1) **ńźŠĽćc**: hiŠĽÉu mŠĽĎi li√™n kŠļŅt `reg0[3]` giŠĽĮa stage 19 v√† 20; nŠļŅu chŠĽČ thŠļ•y stage 19 priority 100 m√† stage 20 priority 100 thiŠļŅu hoŠļ∑c kh√īng match, vŠļ•n ńĎŠĽĀ ŠĽü compile flow. (2) **SŠĽ≠a**: cŠļ∑p stage n√†y kh√īng c√≥ config trŠĽĪc tiŠļŅp; muŠĽĎn thay ńĎŠĽēi behavior, sŠĽ≠a `DHCP_Options.options:server_id`, `lease_time`, etc. ŠĽü stage 19. (3) **Quan s√°t**: `tcpdump -nei tap-vm1 udp port 67 or port 68` thŠļ•y DHCPOFFER quay vŠĽĀ sau DHCPDISCOVER trong < 100ms. (4) **Debug**: khi DHCPOFFER kh√īng emit, d√Ļng `ovn-trace` simulate DHCPDISCOVER, kiŠĽÉm tra (a) stage 19 c√≥ set reg0[3]=1 kh√īng, (b) stage 20 c√≥ match priority 100 kh√īng.

**Ph√Ęn loŠļ°i.** LoŠļ°i stage: **DHCP reply emitter** (subtype "stateful response after option build"). ńźŠĽĎi xŠĽ©ng vŠĽõi `LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS` (stage 19, build payload). C√Ļng hŠĽć vŠĽõi `LS_IN_DHCPV6_RESPONSE` (stage t∆į∆°ng ńĎ∆į∆°ng cho DHCPv6). Kh√°c `LS_IN_ARP_ND_RSP` ŠĽü chŠĽó ARP responder build reply trong 1 stage duy nhŠļ•t (action gŠĽôp), trong khi DHCP t√°ch 2 stage do payload phŠĽ©c tŠļ°p h∆°n.

**Quy tr√¨nh sŠĽ≠ dŠĽ•ng.**
1. TŠļ°o DHCP_Options + LSP (xem ¬ß13.19.5)
2. Verify cŠļ∑p stage compile: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep -E "ls_in_dhcp_(options|response)"` thŠļ•y cŠļ£ 2 priority 100
3. Test full handshake: VM boot ‚Üí tcpdump tap thŠļ•y 4 packet (DISCOVER, OFFER, REQUEST, ACK)
4. Verify timing: DISCOVER ‚Üí OFFER < 100ms (kernel datapath, kh√īng qua userspace)
5. Test failure path: cŠĽĎ t√¨nh set `DHCP_Options.cidr` lŠĽách khŠĽŹi LSP IP ‚Üí DHCPOFFER kh√īng emit (stage 19 fail, stage 20 kh√īng match priority 100)
6. Verify drop counter: `ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=28 | grep "priority=0"` xem n_packets c√≥ tńÉng khi failure path

**Khi xŠļ£y ra sŠĽĪ cŠĽĎ.** Symptom ńĎiŠĽÉn h√¨nh: (a) "VM gŠĽ≠i DHCPDISCOVER nh∆įng kh√īng nhŠļ≠n DHCPOFFER" ‚Üí c√≥ thŠĽÉ stage 19 hoŠļ∑c stage 20. (b) "DHCPOFFER bŠĽč emit nhiŠĽĀu lŠļßn" ‚Üí priority 100 stage 20 tr√Ļng. Diagnostic step-by-step:
- Step 1: tcpdump tap interface VM x√°c nhŠļ≠n c√≥ DHCPDISCOVER ńĎi ra
- Step 2: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_dhcp_options` xem stage 19 priority 100 c√≥ kh√īng + IP ńĎ√ļng
- Step 3: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_dhcp_response` xem stage 20 priority 100 c√≥ kh√īng
- Step 4: `ovn-trace ls1 'inport=="lsp-vm1" && eth.src==aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && ip4.src==0.0.0.0 && ip4.dst==255.255.255.255 && udp.src==68 && udp.dst==67'` ‚ÄĒ xem trace c√≥ ńĎi qua stage 19 (set reg0[3]=1) rŠĽďi stage 20 (match priority 100, output) kh√īng
- Step 5: nŠļŅu stage 19 set reg0[3]=0, root cause ŠĽü build payload (offerip ngo√†i subnet); nŠļŅu stage 20 kh√īng match d√Ļ reg0[3]=1, root cause ŠĽü compile flow (rŠļ•t hiŠļŅm)

Cross-link PhŠļßn 13.10 ¬ßDHCP native + DNS, PhŠļßn 13.18 ¬ßREGBIT_DHCP_OPTS_RESULT, PhŠļßn 20.0 ¬ßVM bootstrap troubleshoot.

**Li√™n quan mŠļ≠t thiŠļŅt.** Tightly coupled: `LS_IN_DHCP_OPTIONS` (stage 19 sibling, build payload), `REGBIT_DHCP_OPTS_RESULT` (`reg0[3]`, cŠļßu nŠĽĎi kŠļŅt quŠļ£), `Logical_Switch_Port.dhcpv4_options` (config trigger), `DHCP_Options.options:server_id` (gi√° trŠĽč ip4.src trong reply), action `put_dhcp_opts` (gŠĽći ŠĽü stage 19 nh∆įng kŠļŅt quŠļ£ ti√™u thŠĽ• ŠĽü stage 20). Loose: `LS_IN_DHCPV6_RESPONSE` (analog cho IPv6), cloud-init (consume IP sau khi stage 20 emit th√†nh c√īng), dnsmasq (alternative external).

**Kh√°c biŠĽát giŠĽĮa c√°c phi√™n bŠļ£n.**
- OVN 2.6 (2016): introduce cŠļ∑p DHCP_OPTIONS / DHCP_RESPONSE t√°ch biŠĽát
- OVN 2.8 (2017): th√™m DHCPV6_RESPONSE analog cho IPv6
- OVN 21.06 (2021): IPAM t√≠ch hŠĽ£p, stage 20 kh√īng thay ńĎŠĽēi nh∆įng stage 19 nhŠļ≠n offerip tŠĽę IPAM
- OVN 22.03 (baseline): stable, stage logic 20 √°nh xŠļ° table 28
- OVN 23.06: th√™m Boot Options support (PXE) qua field `bootfile_name` ŠĽü stage 19, stage 20 emit kh√īng ńĎŠĽēi
- OVN 24.03: tŠĽĎi ∆įu compile khi c√≥ >500 LSP c√≥ dhcpv4_options trong c√Ļng LS

**C√°ch quan s√°t + x√°c minh.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep -A2 "ls_in_dhcp_response"
  table=20 (ls_in_dhcp_response), priority=100,
    match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
           ip4.src == 0.0.0.0 && ip4.dst == 255.255.255.255 &&
           udp.src == 68 && udp.dst == 67 && reg0[3] == 1),
    action=(eth.dst = eth.src; eth.src = aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01;
            ip4.src = 10.0.0.1; ip4.dst = 255.255.255.255;
            udp.src = 67; udp.dst = 68;
            outport = inport; flags.loopback = 1; output;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=28 | head -2
  cookie=0x2, table=28, n_packets=4, in_port=3,udp,tp_src=68,tp_dst=67,reg0=0x8,
    actions=move:NXM_OF_ETH_SRC[]->NXM_OF_ETH_DST[],mod_dl_src:aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01,
            mod_nw_src:10.0.0.1,mod_nw_dst:255.255.255.255,
            mod_tp_src:67,mod_tp_dst:68,output:in_port

$ tcpdump -nei tap-vm1 udp port 67 or port 68
  IP 0.0.0.0.68 > 255.255.255.255.67: BOOTP/DHCP, Request, DHCPDISCOVER
  IP 10.0.0.1.67 > 255.255.255.255.68: BOOTP/DHCP, Reply, DHCPOFFER, lease 3600
  IP 0.0.0.0.68 > 255.255.255.255.67: BOOTP/DHCP, Request, DHCPREQUEST
  IP 10.0.0.1.67 > 255.255.255.255.68: BOOTP/DHCP, Reply, DHCPACK, lease 3600
```

**Source code tham chiŠļŅu.**
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lswitch_dhcp_options_and_response()`: h√†m sinh cŠļ£ stage 19 + 20 (verified branch-22.03)
- `lib/lflow.h` macro `S_SWITCH_IN_DHCP_RESPONSE = 20`
- `controller/lflow.c` dŠĽčch action sequence eth/ip swap xuŠĽĎng OVS
- `lib/actions.c` parser cho REGBIT match expression
- `northd/ovn-northd.8.xml` ¬ß"Ingress Table 20: DHCP response" doc
- Pre-existing reference: ¬ß13.19.5 (cŠļ∑p stage 19), PhŠļßn 13.10 ¬ßDHCP native, PhŠļßn 13.16 d√≤ng 171

**Tr∆įŠĽĚng hŠĽ£p sŠĽĪ cŠĽĎ thŠĽĪc tŠļŅ.** Q2/2025 production OVN 22.03 cluster: tenant deploy 50 VM mŠĽõi, ~30% VM fail boot vŠĽõi "DHCP timeout" sau 60s. Investigation: tcpdump tap interface 1 VM fail thŠļ•y c√≥ DHCPDISCOVER ńĎi ra nh∆įng kh√īng c√≥ DHCPOFFER vŠĽĀ. `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-tenant | grep ls_in_dhcp_options` ‚Üí c√≥ flow priority 100. `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-tenant | grep ls_in_dhcp_response` ‚Üí cŇ©ng c√≥ priority 100. `ovn-trace` simulate DHCPDISCOVER: trace ńĎi v√†o stage 19, gŠĽći `put_dhcp_opts(offerip=192.168.1.55, ...)` nh∆įng `reg0[3]=0` (fail). Root cause: tenant deploy DHCP_Options vŠĽõi `cidr=192.168.1.0/24` cho LS-tenant, nh∆įng IPAM v√ī t√¨nh cŠļ•p IP `192.168.1.55` cho LSP c√≥ MAC tr√Ļng MAC cŇ© cŠĽßa LSP ńĎ√£ xo√° ‚Üí put_dhcp_opts tŠĽę chŠĽĎi v√¨ conflict address. Fix: clear IPAM cache (`ovn-nbctl --wait=hv set Logical_Switch_Port lsp-vm-N addresses="..."` re-set), VM reboot. 100% VM nhŠļ≠n IP. Cross-link PhŠļßn 13.10 ¬ßIPAM conflict.

**B√†i tŠļ≠p synthetic.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-dhcpresp
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-dhcpresp lsp-vm1
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm1 "aa:11:11:11:11:11 10.0.0.5"
DHCP=$(sudo ovn-nbctl create DHCP_Options cidr=10.0.0.0/24 \
       options='"server_id"="10.0.0.1" "lease_time"="3600" "router"="10.0.0.1"')
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-dhcpv4-options lsp-vm1 $DHCP
# Lab task 1: ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-dhcpresp | grep -E "ls_in_dhcp_(options|response)" ‚Üí cŠļ£ 2 priority 100
# Lab task 2: ovn-trace ls-dhcpresp 'inport=="lsp-vm1" && eth.src==aa:11:11:11:11:11 && ip4.src==0.0.0.0 && ip4.dst==255.255.255.255 && udp.src==68 && udp.dst==67' ‚Üí trace pass cŠļ£ stage 19 (reg0[3]=1) + stage 20 (output)
# Lab task 3: BŠļĽ g√£y intentional ‚ÄĒ set DHCP_Options.cidr=192.168.1.0/24 (lŠĽách subnet) ‚Üí trace lŠļ°i, stage 19 ńĎŠļ∑t reg0[3]=0, stage 20 kh√īng match priority 100
# Lab task 4: Restore + remove dhcpv4_options khŠĽŹi lsp-vm1 ‚Üí cŠļ£ 2 stage kh√īng c√≥ flow priority 100 cho VM n√†y
# Lab task 5: tcpdump tap interface VM thŠļ≠t ‚Üí ńĎŠļŅm thŠĽĚi gian DISCOVER ‚Üí OFFER (kŠĽ≥ vŠĽćng < 50ms, kernel datapath)
```

**LŠĽói th∆įŠĽĚng gŠļ∑p + t√≠n hiŠĽáu chŠļ©n ńĎo√°n.**
- Mode A "stage 20 kh√īng match d√Ļ c√≥ flow priority 100": reg0[3] kh√īng bŠļĪng 1 do stage 19 fail ‚Üí check `put_dhcp_opts` argument trong lflow-list
- Mode B "DHCPOFFER emit nh∆įng client tŠĽę chŠĽĎi": ip4.src kh√īng phŠļ£i server_id m√† client expect ‚Üí kiŠĽÉm tra `DHCP_Options.options:server_id`
- Mode C "DHCPOFFER bŠĽč flood ra port kh√°c": flow stage 20 thiŠļŅu `outport = inport` action ‚Üí recompile northd
- Mode D "DHCPOFFER c√≥ MAC src lŠļ°": eth.src kh√īng khŠĽõp vŠĽõi gateway MAC ‚Üí audit `DHCP_Options.options:router` c√Ļng `LR_IN_IP_INPUT`
- Mode E "Latency cao DISCOVER ‚Üí OFFER >500ms": packet ńĎi qua userspace controller thay v√¨ kernel fast path ‚Üí `ovs-vswitchd` log c√≥ "upcall" message ‚Üí restart ovs-vswitchd hoŠļ∑c n√Ęng OVS ‚Č• 2.7 cho optimized path

**So s√°nh vŠĽõi hŠĽá kh√°c.** Linux dnsmasq DHCP server: monolithic process xŠĽ≠ l√Ĺ cŠļ£ parse request + build payload + emit reply trong c√Ļng userspace handler; OVN t√°ch 2 stage trong kernel datapath cho ph√©p compose vŠĽõi pipeline kh√°c (e.g., ACL √°p tr∆įŠĽõc DHCP nŠļŅu cŠļßn). ISC DHCP: 2 phase t∆į∆°ng tŠĽĪ (server build packet ‚Üí kernel send) nh∆įng ŠĽü userspace. Cisco IOS `ip dhcp pool`: monolithic, kh√īng t√°ch stage. AWS DHCP option set: managed, kh√īng expose pipeline. So vŠĽõi cŠļ∑p `LS_IN_ARP_ND_RSP` (1 stage trong OVN cho ARP), DHCP t√°ch 2 stage do payload DHCP c√≥ 6+ option phŠļ£i build, kh√īng thŠĽÉ fit trong 1 action sequence.

---

## ¬ß13.19.23 LS_OUT_PRE_LB ‚ÄĒ chuŠļ©n bŠĽč conntrack zone cho egress LB return path

**Kh√°i niŠĽám.** `LS_OUT_PRE_LB` l√† stage logic egress ńĎŠļßu ti√™n cŠĽßa LS pipeline (sau khi packet ńĎi qua LS_IN_L2_LKUP v√† rŠļĹ v√†o nh√°nh egress), ńĎ√≥ng vai tr√≤ **chuŠļ©n bŠĽč conntrack** tr∆įŠĽõc khi stage `LS_OUT_LB` (nŠļŅu c√≥) thŠĽĪc hiŠĽán reverse-DNAT cho reply traffic LB. Stage n√†y gŠĽći `ct_next` (load conntrack state v√†o ct_state register) hoŠļ∑c set REGBIT ńĎŠĽÉ stage downstream biŠļŅt packet ńĎ√£ ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c conntrack-tracked. ńźŠĽĎi xŠĽ©ng vŠĽõi `LS_IN_PRE_LB` ŠĽü chiŠĽĀu ingress; c√Ļng nhau form pair tŠļ°o bidirectional LB stateful semantics. LoŠļ°i: **stateful conntrack preparer egress**, sub-loŠļ°i "egress LB context loader".

**LŠĽčch sŠĽ≠ + bŠĽĎi cŠļ£nh.** Stage c√≥ mŠļ∑t tŠĽę OVN 2.7 (2017) khi LB stateful trong OVN ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c Numan Siddique implement ńĎŠļßy ńĎŠĽß. Tr∆įŠĽõc OVN 2.7, LB chŠĽČ stateless (DNAT trŠĽĪc tiŠļŅp kh√īng conntrack), n√™n kh√īng cŠļßn stage chuŠļ©n bŠĽč. OVN 2.7 th√™m conntrack zone cho LB ‚Üí cŠļßn stage `PRE_LB` ŠĽü cŠļ£ ingress v√† egress ńĎŠĽÉ load state v√†o pipeline. OVN 21.06 ńĎŠļ°i tu LB hŠĽó trŠĽ£ affinity ‚Üí stage `PRE_LB` egress ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c tinh chŠĽČnh ńĎŠĽÉ kh√īng xung ńĎŠĽôt vŠĽõi affinity zone. OVN 22.03 (baseline) ŠĽēn ńĎŠĽčnh, stage logic 1 trong egress pipeline.

**VŠĽč tr√≠ trong kiŠļŅn tr√ļc.** Stage logic 1 trong LS_OUT pipeline, √°nh xŠļ° OF table 41 tr√™n br-int (theo 13.16 d√≤ng 194). ńźŠĽ©ng ńĎŠļßu egress pipeline, sau khi packet ńĎ√£ rŠĽĚi ingress qua `LS_IN_L2_LKUP` output. Tr∆įŠĽõc `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` (stage 2) v√† `LS_OUT_LB` (stage t∆į∆°ng ńĎ∆į∆°ng ingress LB nh∆įng cho reply path). Scope: per-packet, per-LS datapath, chŠĽČ packet egress (ńĎ√£ set outport, sŠļĮp ńĎi ra LSP ńĎ√≠ch).

**Vai tr√≤.** Vai tr√≤ ch√≠nh: **load conntrack state** tŠĽę zone LB v√†o `ct_state` register cho packet reply (server ‚Üí client) ńĎŠĽÉ stage `LS_OUT_LB` c√≥ thŠĽÉ reverse-DNAT (ńĎŠĽēi src tŠĽę backend IP vŠĽĀ VIP). Vai tr√≤ phŠĽ•: chuŠļ©n bŠĽč REGBIT cho stage egress ACL biŠļŅt packet thuŠĽôc connection LB n√†o. PhŠļ°m vi vai tr√≤: chŠĽČ packet c√≥ khŠļ£ nńÉng l√† reply cŠĽßa LB connection; non-LB traffic ńĎi qua bypass priority 0 next.

**V√¨ sao sinh ra.** Pre-existence pain: LB stateless trong OVN 2.6 v√† sŠĽõm h∆°n chŠĽČ DNAT chiŠĽĀu client ‚Üí backend, kh√īng track reply backend ‚Üí client. Reply phŠļ£i dŠĽĪa v√†o routing th√īng th∆įŠĽĚng m√† kh√īng c√≥ context "ńĎ√Ęy l√† reply cŠĽßa LB connection" ‚Üí khi client query VIP=10.0.0.100, backend reply src=10.0.0.5 ńĎŠļŅn client; client thŠļ•y IP lŠļ° (kh√īng phŠļ£i VIP) ‚Üí reject. Solution: bidirectional LB vŠĽõi conntrack zone ‚ÄĒ chiŠĽĀu forward DNAT VIP‚Üíbackend ŠĽü `LS_IN_LB`, l∆įu mapping v√†o conntrack; chiŠĽĀu reply UN-DNAT backend‚ÜíVIP ŠĽü `LS_OUT_LB`. ńźŠĽÉ `LS_OUT_LB` biŠļŅt phŠļ£i UN-DNAT, cŠļßn `LS_OUT_PRE_LB` load state tr∆įŠĽõc.

**VŠļ•n ńĎŠĽĀ giŠļ£i quyŠļŅt.** CŠĽ• thŠĽÉ: (a) packet egress c√≥ src = backend IP, dst = client IP, (b) cŠļßn biŠļŅt packet n√†y c√≥ phŠļ£i reply cŠĽßa LB connection kh√īng, (c) nŠļŅu phŠļ£i, cŠļßn UN-DNAT ńĎŠĽÉ client thŠļ•y src = VIP. C√°ch giŠļ£i: priority 110 flow `match=(ip)` action `reg0[2] = 1; ct_next;` ‚ÄĒ set REGBIT_CONNTRACK_NAT (`reg0[2]`) b√°o stage egress LB c√≥ thŠĽÉ UN-NAT, ńĎŠĽďng thŠĽĚi `ct_next` load ct_state v√†o register tŠĽę conntrack zone ńĎ√£ setup ŠĽü ingress. Priority 0 flow `match=(1)` action `next;` cho non-IP traffic. PhŠļ°m vi: stateful LB only.

**TŠļßm quan trŠĽćng.** MŠĽ©c trung b√¨nh. BŠļĮt buŠĽôc cho LB stateful (default tŠĽę OVN 2.7+); nŠļŅu disable, reply path tŠĽę backend kh√īng UN-DNAT, client tŠĽę chŠĽĎi. Engineer must-know: hiŠĽÉu `LS_OUT_PRE_LB` l√† cŠļ∑p ńĎ√īi vŠĽõi `LS_IN_PRE_LB` v√† l√† dependency cŠĽßa `LS_OUT_LB`; nŠļŅu egress LB kh√īng hoŠļ°t ńĎŠĽông, kiŠĽÉm tra stage 1 egress tr∆įŠĽõc stage 5 (LB).

**C∆° chŠļŅ hoŠļ°t ńĎŠĽông.** H√†m sinh flow: `build_lswitch_lb_egress()` (ńĎ√īi khi gŠĽći l√† `build_pre_lb()` chung cho cŠļ£ ingress v√† egress trong c√°c phi√™n bŠļ£n cŇ©) trong `northd/northd.c` (verified branch-22.03). H√†m chŠĽČ sinh flow nŠļŅu LS c√≥ √≠t nhŠļ•t mŠĽôt LB attached:

```
table=41 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=110,
  match=(ip),
  action=(reg0[2] = 1; ct_next;)

table=41 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=100,
  match=(nd || nd_rs || nd_ra || mldv1 || mldv2),
  action=(next;)

table=41 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=110,
  match=(eth.dst == ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff || eth.mcast),
  action=(next;)

table=41 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=0,
  match=(1), action=(next;)
```

Flow priority 110 exclude broadcast/multicast/IPv6 ND ńĎŠĽÉ kh√īng gŠĽći conntrack cho traffic kh√īng cŠļßn (tr√°nh overhead v√† race condition vŠĽõi ND responder). Flow priority 0 default cho LS kh√īng c√≥ LB (`has_lb_vip=false`), khi ńĎ√≥ stage skip ho√†n to√†n. Action `ct_next` l√† OVN extended action, controller dŠĽčch xuŠĽĎng OVS `ct(table=Next, zone=NXM_NX_REG13[16..31])` ‚ÄĒ REG13 high half l√† LB zone. Sau stage n√†y, packet c√≥ ct_state populated, sŠļĶn s√†ng cho `LS_OUT_LB` UN-DNAT.

**C√°ch kŠĽĻ s∆į vŠļ≠n h√†nh th√†nh thŠļ°o.** (1) **ńźŠĽćc**: hiŠĽÉu `reg0[2]` l√† REGBIT_CONNTRACK_NAT b√°o cho egress LB UN-NAT; ph√Ęn biŠĽát vŠĽõi `reg0[0]` (REGBIT_CONNTRACK_DEFRAG) v√† `reg0[1]` (REGBIT_CONNTRACK_COMMIT). (2) **SŠĽ≠a**: stage n√†y kh√īng c√≥ config trŠĽĪc tiŠļŅp; chŠĽČ k√≠ch hoŠļ°t khi LS c√≥ LB attach. `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add ls1 lb-web` ‚Üí stage n√†y sŠļĹ c√≥ flow priority 110. (3) **Quan s√°t**: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_pre_lb` xem c√≥ flow priority 110 kh√īng. (4) **Debug**: nŠļŅu reply LB kh√īng UN-DNAT, d√Ļng `ofproto/trace` simulate reply packet (src=backend, dst=client), kiŠĽÉm tra stage 41 c√≥ set reg0[2]=1 v√† ct_next c√≥ load ct_state ńĎ√ļng kh√īng.

**Ph√Ęn loŠļ°i.** LoŠļ°i stage: **conntrack preparer egress** (subtype "egress LB context loader"). ńźŠĽĎi xŠĽ©ng `LS_IN_PRE_LB` (ingress side, prepare cho forward DNAT). Kh√°c `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` (cŇ©ng pre-stateful nh∆įng cho ACL context). C√Ļng hŠĽć "stateful preparer" vŠĽõi `LR_IN_DEFRAG`, `LS_IN_PRE_STATEFUL`.

**Quy tr√¨nh sŠĽ≠ dŠĽ•ng.**
1. TŠļ°o LB + LS: `ovn-nbctl lb-add lb-web "10.0.0.100:80" "10.0.0.5:80,10.0.0.6:80"` + `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add ls1 lb-web`
2. Verify stage egress compile: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_pre_lb` thŠļ•y priority 110 + 0
3. Test forward path: client (10.0.0.20) curl VIP (10.0.0.100) ‚Üí tcpdump tap backend thŠļ•y packet vŠĽõi src=10.0.0.20, dst=10.0.0.5 (DNAT bŠĽüi LS_IN_LB)
4. Test reply path: backend reply ‚Üí tcpdump tap client thŠļ•y src=10.0.0.100 (UN-DNAT, kŠļŅt quŠļ£ cŠĽßa LS_OUT_PRE_LB + LS_OUT_LB)
5. Verify conntrack zone: `dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=<lb_zone>` thŠļ•y entry vŠĽõi orig=client‚ÜíVIP, reply=backend‚Üíclient
6. Disable LB: `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-del ls1 lb-web` ‚Üí stage chŠĽČ c√≤n priority 0 default

**Khi xŠļ£y ra sŠĽĪ cŠĽĎ.** Symptom ńĎiŠĽÉn h√¨nh: (a) "Client gŠĽ≠i request ńĎŠļŅn VIP nhŠļ≠n reply vŠĽĀ src=backend thay v√¨ VIP, tŠĽę chŠĽĎi connection" ‚Üí suspect stage egress UN-DNAT chain (PRE_LB + LB). (b) "Reply latency cao gŠļ•p 10 lŠļßn forward" ‚Üí conntrack zone exhaustion. Diagnostic:
- Step 1: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_pre_lb` x√°c nhŠļ≠n flow priority 110 tŠĽďn tŠļ°i
- Step 2: `ofproto/trace br-int 'in_port=tap-backend,ip,ip_src=10.0.0.5,ip_dst=10.0.0.20,...'` simulate reply, xem stage 41 c√≥ set reg0[2]=1 + ct_next kh√īng
- Step 3: nŠļŅu trace bypass stage 41 (ńĎi thŠļ≥ng table 0), kiŠĽÉm tra LS c√≥ attach LB kh√īng
- Step 4: `dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=<lb_zone>` xem entry c√≥ tŠĽďn tŠļ°i kh√īng (forward ńĎ√£ commit)
- Step 5: `cat /proc/sys/net/netfilter/nf_conntrack_count` xem zone c√≥ exhaust kh√īng

Cross-link PhŠļßn 13.3 ¬ßLB stateful, PhŠļßn 19.0 ¬ßLB asymmetric debug.

**Li√™n quan mŠļ≠t thiŠļŅt.** Tightly coupled: `LS_IN_PRE_LB` (ingress sibling), `LS_OUT_LB` (downstream consumer, UN-DNAT), `Load_Balancer.vips` (config trigger), `REGBIT_CONNTRACK_NAT` (`reg0[2]`), conntrack zone LB (REG13[16..31]). Loose: `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` (c√Ļng kiŠĽÉu stateful preparer nh∆įng cho ACL), `LS_IN_LB_AFF_*` (affinity zone, kh√°c zone vŠĽõi LB ch√≠nh).

**Kh√°c biŠĽát giŠĽĮa c√°c phi√™n bŠļ£n.**
- OVN 2.7 (2017): introduce stage c√Ļng LB stateful
- OVN 20.06: t√°ch r√Ķ ingress vs egress PRE_LB (tr∆įŠĽõc ńĎ√≥ d√Ļng chung 1 h√†m)
- OVN 21.06: th√™m ND/multicast exclude flows
- OVN 22.03 (baseline): stable, stage logic 1 √°nh xŠļ° table 41
- OVN 23.06: tŠĽĎi ∆įu compile khi LS c√≥ 100+ LB attach
- OVN 24.03: th√™m fragment handling cho UDP LB (interaction vŠĽõi defrag stage)

**C√°ch quan s√°t + x√°c minh.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep -A2 "ls_out_pre_lb"
  table=1 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=110,
    match=(ip),
    action=(reg0[2] = 1; ct_next;)
  table=1 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=110,
    match=(eth.dst == ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff || eth.mcast),
    action=(next;)
  table=1 (ls_out_pre_lb), priority=0,
    match=(1), action=(next;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=41 | head -3
  cookie=0x3, table=41, n_packets=128, ip,metadata=0x4,
    actions=load:0x1->NXM_NX_XXREG0[66],ct(table=42,zone=NXM_NX_REG13[16..31])

$ ovs-appctl dpctl/dump-conntrack zone=<lb_zone> | head -3
  tcp,orig=(src=10.0.0.20,dst=10.0.0.100,sport=4001,dport=80),
       reply=(src=10.0.0.5,dst=10.0.0.20,sport=80,dport=4001),
       protoinfo=(state=ESTABLISHED), zone=<lb_zone>
```

**Source code tham chiŠļŅu.**
- `northd/northd.c` `build_lswitch_lb_egress()`: h√†m ch√≠nh (hoŠļ∑c `build_pre_lb()` cŇ©; verified branch-22.03)
- `lib/lflow.h` macro `S_SWITCH_OUT_PRE_LB = 1` (egress stage 1)
- `lib/actions.c` parser `ct_next` action
- `controller/lflow.c` dŠĽčch ct_next xuŠĽĎng OVS `ct(table=Next, zone=...)`
- `northd/ovn-northd.8.xml` ¬ß"Egress Table 1: Pre LB" doc
- Pre-existing reference: ¬ß13.19.4 (LS_IN_LB ingress), PhŠļßn 13.16 d√≤ng 194

**Tr∆įŠĽĚng hŠĽ£p sŠĽĪ cŠĽĎ thŠĽĪc tŠļŅ.** Q3/2024 production OVN 22.03 cluster: customer report "client connect VIP web-vip th√†nh c√īng TCP handshake nh∆įng kh√īng nhŠļ≠n response data, connection timeout sau 60s". Investigation: tcpdump tap interface client thŠļ•y SYN-ACK vŠĽĀ vŠĽõi src=10.0.0.5 (backend IP, kh√īng phŠļ£i VIP 10.0.0.100). Customer expect SYN-ACK src=VIP. `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-web | grep ls_out_pre_lb` trŠĽĎng ‚ÄĒ kh√īng c√≥ flow priority 110. `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-list ls-web` ‚Üí trŠĽĎng. Root cause: customer attach LB v√†o LR thay v√¨ LS (`ovn-nbctl lr-lb-add lr-pub lb-web`), nh∆įng client connect qua east-west traffic trong c√Ļng LS-web ‚Üí LB kh√īng ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c √°p ŠĽü LR (v√¨ traffic kh√īng ńĎi qua router), trong khi LS kh√īng c√≥ LB attach ‚Üí stage `LS_OUT_PRE_LB` kh√īng sinh flow priority 110, reply kh√īng UN-DNAT. Fix: `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add ls-web lb-web` (attach LB v√†o cŠļ£ LS ńĎŠĽÉ east-west work). Sau fix, flow priority 110 xuŠļ•t hiŠĽán, reply ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c UN-DNAT th√†nh VIP. Connection success. Cross-link PhŠļßn 13.3 ¬ßLB attach point (LS vs LR).

**B√†i tŠļ≠p synthetic.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-prelb
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-prelb lsp-client
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-prelb lsp-be1
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-prelb lsp-be2
sudo ovn-nbctl lb-add lb-prelb-test "10.0.0.100:80" "10.0.0.5:80,10.0.0.6:80"
# Lab task 1 (ch∆įa attach LB): ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-prelb | grep ls_out_pre_lb ‚Üí chŠĽČ priority 0
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add ls-prelb lb-prelb-test
# Lab task 2 (sau attach): ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-prelb | grep ls_out_pre_lb ‚Üí c√≥ priority 110
# Lab task 3: ofproto/trace 'in_port=lsp-be1,ip,ip_src=10.0.0.5,ip_dst=10.0.0.20,...' ‚Üí trace pass stage 41 set reg0[2]=1
# Lab task 4: chŠļ°y actual traffic client ‚Üí VIP, tcpdump tap client xem src trong reply (kŠĽ≥ vŠĽćng 10.0.0.100 sau khi cŠļ£ PRE_LB + LB egress chŠļ°y)
# Lab task 5: detach LB ‚Üí verify flow priority 110 biŠļŅn mŠļ•t + traffic break
```

**LŠĽói th∆įŠĽĚng gŠļ∑p + t√≠n hiŠĽáu chŠļ©n ńĎo√°n.**
- Mode A "stage kh√īng c√≥ flow priority 110": LS kh√īng c√≥ LB attach ‚Üí `ovn-nbctl ls-lb-add` ńĎŠĽÉ attach
- Mode B "reply kh√īng UN-DNAT d√Ļ c√≥ flow priority 110": `LS_OUT_LB` (stage downstream) thiŠļŅu hoŠļ∑c compile lŠĽói ‚Üí check stage egress LB
- Mode C "conntrack zone exhaustion": nhiŠĽĀu LB share c√Ļng zone REG13[16..31] ‚Üí tńÉng `nf_conntrack_max` hoŠļ∑c t√°ch zone
- Mode D "reply latency cao": ct_next miss, packet bŠĽč punt userspace ‚Üí kiŠĽÉm tra ovs-vswitchd log "upcall"
- Mode E "ND/multicast bŠĽč conntrack-track kh√īng cŠļßn thiŠļŅt": flow priority 110 cho `eth.mcast` match `next` thiŠļŅu ‚Üí recompile northd

**So s√°nh vŠĽõi hŠĽá kh√°c.** Linux iptables `-j CT --zone N` analog: chuŠļ©n bŠĽč conntrack zone tr∆įŠĽõc stateful module; nh∆įng iptables kh√īng c√≥ concept "egress pipeline" r√Ķ r√†ng (chŠĽČ c√≥ chain POSTROUTING). HAProxy kh√īng cŠļßn stage chuŠļ©n bŠĽč t∆į∆°ng ńĎ∆į∆°ng v√¨ HAProxy l√† proxy L7 giŠĽĮ session state trong userspace. NSX-T edge transport node: distributed LB t∆į∆°ng tŠĽĪ OVN nh∆įng stage prepare Šļ©n trong NSX kernel module, kh√īng expose pipeline API. Cisco ACI service graph: redirect-and-track pattern t∆į∆°ng ńĎ∆į∆°ng semantic. AWS NLB: managed, kh√īng expose internal stage; reply UN-DNAT happens transparent.

---

## ¬ß13.19.24 LS_OUT_ACL ‚ÄĒ ńĎ√°nh gi√° ACL stateful tr√™n chiŠĽĀu egress cŠĽßa LS

**Kh√°i niŠĽám.** `LS_OUT_ACL` l√† stage logic egress ńĎ√°nh gi√° danh s√°ch Access Control List cŠĽßa Logical_Switch theo direction `to-lport` (packet sŠļĮp ra LSP ńĎ√≠ch). ńźŠĽĎi xŠĽ©ng vŠĽõi `LS_IN_ACL` (¬ß13.19.3) ŠĽü chiŠĽĀu ingress nh∆įng ńĎ√°nh gi√° khi packet ńĎ√£ chŠĽćn ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c outport v√† sŠļĮp ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c delivery. MŠĽói ACL row trong NBDB c√≥ `direction=to-lport` ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c compile xuŠĽĎng stage n√†y th√†nh Logical_Flow vŠĽõi match expression CIDR/L4 + action `allow`/`allow-related`/`drop`/`reject`. SŠĽ≠ dŠĽ•ng ńĎŠĽÉ filter traffic ńĎi v√†o LSP cŠĽ• thŠĽÉ (v√≠ dŠĽ•: ngńÉn VM cŠĽ• thŠĽÉ nhŠļ≠n traffic tŠĽę subnet b√™n ngo√†i). LoŠļ°i: **stateful ACL evaluator egress**, sub-loŠļ°i "to-lport filter".

**LŠĽčch sŠĽ≠ + bŠĽĎi cŠļ£nh.** Stage c√≥ mŠļ∑t tŠĽę OVN 2.5 (2016) c√Ļng vŠĽõi ACL framework ńĎŠļßu ti√™n. Tr∆įŠĽõc ńĎ√≥, OVN kh√īng c√≥ ACL native, phŠļ£i dŠĽĪa v√†o iptables external. OVN 2.7 th√™m `allow-related` semantic (stateful) qua `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` + `LS_OUT_ACL` cŠļ∑p ńĎ√īi. OVN 21.06 ńĎŠļ°i tu ACL vŠĽõi `apply-after-lb` option ńĎŠĽÉ ACL √°p sau LB stage (egress). OVN 22.03 (baseline) ŠĽēn ńĎŠĽčnh, stage logic 4 trong egress pipeline. OVN 24.03 hŠĽó trŠĽ£ ACL tier (priority cao h∆°n cho ACL hŠĽá thŠĽĎng).

**VŠĽč tr√≠ trong kiŠļŅn tr√ļc.** Stage logic 4 trong LS_OUT pipeline, √°nh xŠļ° OF table 44 tr√™n br-int (theo 13.16 d√≤ng 137 v√† 197). ńźŠĽ©ng sau `LS_OUT_PRE_LB` (stage 1), `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` (stage 2), `LS_OUT_PRE_STATEFUL` (stage 3) v√† tr∆įŠĽõc `LS_OUT_LB` (stage 5+) c√Ļng `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2` (stage 9). Scope: per-packet, per-LS datapath, per-ACL row c√≥ `direction=to-lport`. Stage chŠļ°y tr√™n chassis cŠĽßa LSP ńĎ√≠ch (chassis n∆°i packet sŠļĮp ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c output).

**Vai tr√≤.** Vai tr√≤ ch√≠nh: **filter traffic ńĎi v√†o LSP ńĎ√≠ch** dŠĽĪa tr√™n 5-tuple + ACL match expression. Vai tr√≤ phŠĽ•: vŠĽõi `allow-related`, commit conntrack entry ńĎŠĽÉ reply path ng∆įŠĽ£c chiŠĽĀu (LS_IN_ACL) cho ph√©p. PhŠļ°m vi vai tr√≤: chŠĽČ ACL c√≥ `direction=to-lport`; ACL `direction=from-lport` ńĎ√°nh gi√° ŠĽü `LS_IN_ACL` (ingress). Stage stateful nŠļŅu c√≥ ACL `allow-related` hoŠļ∑c `reject`, stateless nŠļŅu chŠĽČ c√≥ `allow`/`drop`.

**V√¨ sao sinh ra.** Pre-existence pain: OVN 2.4 kh√īng c√≥ ACL ‚Üí security policy phŠļ£i dŠĽĪa v√†o iptables tr√™n hypervisor host (per-VM iptables rules) ‚Üí quŠļ£n l√Ĺ phŠĽ©c tŠļ°p + kh√īng declarative + kh√īng follow VM khi migrate. Solution: ACL native trong OVN vŠĽõi 2 direction (`from-lport` filter outbound, `to-lport` filter inbound) ‚Üí declarative qua NBDB, follow VM migrate, stateful qua conntrack zone OVS. `LS_OUT_ACL` cŠĽ• thŠĽÉ giŠļ£i quyŠļŅt pain "filter inbound traffic v√†o VM" m√† ingress stage kh√īng ph√Ļ hŠĽ£p (v√¨ `LS_IN_ACL` ńĎ√°nh gi√° khi packet v√†o LS, ch∆įa biŠļŅt outport cŠĽ• thŠĽÉ).

**VŠļ•n ńĎŠĽĀ giŠļ£i quyŠļŅt.** CŠĽ• thŠĽÉ: (a) packet ńĎ√£ v√†o LS, ńĎ√£ chŠĽćn outport (LSP ńĎ√≠ch), (b) cŠļßn kiŠĽÉm tra packet n√†y c√≥ ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c ph√©p v√†o LSP ńĎ√≥ kh√īng, (c) c√≥ thŠĽÉ commit conntrack ńĎŠĽÉ reply ng∆įŠĽ£c chiŠĽĀu cho ph√©p. C√°ch giŠļ£i: ACL row `direction=to-lport,priority=2000,match="outport == \"lsp-vm\" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.0/24",action=allow-related` ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c compile th√†nh flow priority `2000+OVN_ACL_PRI_OFFSET`:

```
table=44 (ls_out_acl), priority=4000,
  match=(reg0[10] == 1 && (outport == "lsp-vm" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.0/24)),
  action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;) /* allow-related: commit ct, allow */

table=44 (ls_out_acl), priority=2000,
  match=(reg0[7] == 1 && (outport == "lsp-vm" && ip4.src == 192.168.0.0/16)),
  action=(/* drop */)

table=44 (ls_out_acl), priority=1,
  match=(ip), action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;) /* default allow if no ACL match */

table=44 (ls_out_acl), priority=0,
  match=(1), action=(next;)
```

REGBIT `reg0[10]` = ACL_HINT_ALLOW_REL (set bŠĽüi `LS_OUT_ACL_HINT` stage 3 tr∆įŠĽõc ńĎ√≥), `reg0[7]` = ACL_HINT_DROP. Action `allow-related` set `reg0[1] = 1` (REGBIT_CONNTRACK_COMMIT) b√°o stage `LS_OUT_LB` hoŠļ∑c `LS_OUT_DELIVERY` commit conntrack. PhŠļ°m vi giŠļ£i quyŠļŅt: ACL filtering inbound v√†o LSP vŠĽõi stateful semantics.

**TŠļßm quan trŠĽćng.** MŠĽ©c trung b√¨nh. BŠļĮt buŠĽôc cho mŠĽći triŠĽÉn khai c√≥ security policy native (OpenStack security group, K8s NetworkPolicy mapped sang OVN ACL). NŠļŅu disable hoŠļ∑c kh√īng c√≥ ACL, traffic tŠĽĪ do v√†o VM. Engineer must-know: hiŠĽÉu cŠļ∑p `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` + `LS_OUT_ACL` t∆į∆°ng ńĎ∆į∆°ng `LS_IN_PRE_ACL` + `LS_IN_ACL` ŠĽü ingress; biŠļŅt direction `to-lport` vs `from-lport` quyŠļŅt ńĎŠĽčnh ACL √°p ŠĽü stage n√†o.

**C∆° chŠļŅ hoŠļ°t ńĎŠĽông.** H√†m sinh flow: `build_acls()` trong `northd/northd.c` (verified branch-22.03, d√≤ng 6688+) vŠĽõi chŠļŅ ńĎŠĽô filter `direction == "to-lport"` cho stage egress. H√†m gŠĽći `consider_acl()` cho mŠĽói ACL row, chŠĽćn stage compile dŠĽĪa tr√™n `direction` + `options:apply-after-lb`:
- `direction=from-lport` ‚Üí compile v√†o `LS_IN_ACL` (ingress)
- `direction=to-lport` + `apply-after-lb=false` (default) ‚Üí compile v√†o `LS_OUT_ACL` (egress, stage n√†y)
- `direction=to-lport` + `apply-after-lb=true` ‚Üí compile v√†o `LS_OUT_ACL_AFTER_LB` (stage egress cho post-LB filtering)

MŠĽói ACL row sinh 1 flow stage egress ACL vŠĽõi:
- `priority = ACL.priority + OVN_ACL_PRI_OFFSET` (default offset 2000)
- `match = "<ACL_HINT_REGBIT> && (<ACL.match expression>)"`
- `action = <action sequence>` tuŠĽ≥ `ACL.action` (allow ‚Üí next; allow-related ‚Üí reg0[1]=1; next; drop ‚Üí drop; reject ‚Üí tcp_reset/icmp_unreachable + drop)

Stage cŇ©ng c√≥ flow default priority 1 (allow nŠļŅu kh√īng match ACL, cho ACL whitelist semantic) v√† priority 0 fallback.

**C√°ch kŠĽĻ s∆į vŠļ≠n h√†nh th√†nh thŠļ°o.** (1) **ńźŠĽćc**: ph√Ęn biŠĽát direction `from-lport` (ńĎ√°nh gi√° ŠĽü `LS_IN_ACL`) vs `to-lport` (ńĎ√°nh gi√° ŠĽü `LS_OUT_ACL`); biŠļŅt ACL_HINT REGBIT (`reg0[7..10]`). (2) **SŠĽ≠a**: `ovn-nbctl acl-add ls1 to-lport 2000 'outport == "lsp-vm" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.0/24' allow-related` ńĎŠĽÉ add ACL inbound. (3) **Quan s√°t**: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_acl` ńĎŠļŅm sŠĽĎ flow per priority. (4) **Debug**: nŠļŅu traffic bŠĽč drop d√Ļ ACL allow, d√Ļng `ovn-trace` hoŠļ∑c `ofproto/trace` simulate packet egress, xem stage 44 c√≥ match ACL allow priority cao kh√īng.

**Ph√Ęn loŠļ°i.** LoŠļ°i stage: **stateful ACL evaluator** (subtype "to-lport filter"). ńźŠĽĎi xŠĽ©ng `LS_IN_ACL` (ingress, from-lport). Kh√°c `LS_OUT_ACL_AFTER_LB` (post-LB filter cho c√Ļng to-lport nh∆įng sau stage LB). C√Ļng hŠĽć "stateful evaluator" vŠĽõi `LS_IN_ACL`, `LR_IN_ACL` (nŠļŅu c√≥).

**Quy tr√¨nh sŠĽ≠ dŠĽ•ng.**
1. TŠļ°o LS + LSP: `ovn-nbctl ls-add ls1 && ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls1 lsp-vm-victim`
2. Add ACL inbound deny: `ovn-nbctl acl-add ls1 to-lport 2000 'outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 192.168.0.0/16' drop`
3. Add ACL inbound allow specific: `ovn-nbctl acl-add ls1 to-lport 2500 'outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.5' allow-related`
4. Verify compile: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_acl` thŠļ•y 2 flow priority 4500 (allow-related) + 4000 (drop) + default
5. Test: client 10.0.0.5 ‚Üí lsp-vm-victim PASS; client 192.168.0.10 ‚Üí lsp-vm-victim DROP
6. Verify reply path: client 10.0.0.5 ńĎ√£ PASS, reply ng∆įŠĽ£c chiŠĽĀu phŠļ£i PASS (do allow-related commit ct entry, `LS_IN_ACL` allow ct.est && !ct.rpl)

**Khi xŠļ£y ra sŠĽĪ cŠĽĎ.** Symptom ńĎiŠĽÉn h√¨nh: (a) "VM-A gŠĽ≠i ńĎŠļŅn VM-B trong c√Ļng LS, packet ńĎŠļŅn nh∆įng VM-B kh√īng nhŠļ≠n (drop ŠĽü egress)" ‚Üí suspect ACL `to-lport` deny. (b) "VM nhŠļ≠n traffic kh√īng mong muŠĽĎn tŠĽę subnet kh√īng cho ph√©p" ‚Üí ACL `to-lport` thiŠļŅu drop rule. Diagnostic:
- Step 1: `ovn-nbctl acl-list ls1 | grep to-lport` xem ACL inbound ńĎ√£ config ńĎ√ļng ch∆įa
- Step 2: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_acl` xem flow priority sinh ńĎ√ļng kh√īng
- Step 3: `ovn-trace ls1 'inport=="lsp-A" && eth.src==<MAC-A> && ip4.src==<IP-A> && ip4.dst==<IP-B> && tcp.dst==80'` ‚ÄĒ xem trace c√≥ hit drop ŠĽü stage 44 kh√īng
- Step 4: nŠļŅu hit drop, x√°c ńĎŠĽčnh ACL row g√Ęy drop bŠļĪng priority: lflow-list hiŠĽÉn thŠĽč priority + match expression
- Step 5: `dpctl/dump-conntrack` xem ct entry c√≥ commit kh√īng (cho debug allow-related semantics)

Cross-link PhŠļßn 13.3 ¬ßACL framework, PhŠļßn 19.0 ¬ßACL drop debug, PhŠļßn 9.24 ¬ßct_state.

**Li√™n quan mŠļ≠t thiŠļŅt.** Tightly coupled: NBDB `ACL` table vŠĽõi column `direction=to-lport`, `LS_OUT_PRE_ACL` (stage 2 sibling, prepare ct), `LS_OUT_PRE_STATEFUL` (stage 3, set ACL_HINT REGBIT), `LS_IN_ACL` (ńĎŠĽĎi xŠĽ©ng ingress), action `allow-related` (set reg0[1]), conntrack zone ACL (REG13[0..15]). Loose: `Port_Group` (hŠĽó trŠĽ£ match expression c√≥ `outport == @pg_name`), `LS_OUT_ACL_AFTER_LB` (stage egress post-LB cho c√Ļng to-lport).

**Kh√°c biŠĽát giŠĽĮa c√°c phi√™n bŠļ£n.**
- OVN 2.5 (2016): introduce stage c√Ļng ACL framework
- OVN 2.7: th√™m `allow-related` semantic stateful
- OVN 21.06: th√™m `apply-after-lb` option, t√°ch stage `LS_OUT_ACL_AFTER_LB`
- OVN 22.03 (baseline): stable, stage logic 4 √°nh xŠļ° table 44
- OVN 23.06: th√™m `reject` action vŠĽõi ICMP unreachable response
- OVN 24.03: th√™m ACL tier (priority cao h∆°n cho ACL hŠĽá thŠĽĎng vs user)

**C√°ch quan s√°t + x√°c minh.**

```
$ ovn-nbctl acl-list ls1
  to-lport  2500 (outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.5)  allow-related
  to-lport  2000 (outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 192.168.0.0/16)  drop

$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep -A2 "ls_out_acl"
  table=4 (ls_out_acl), priority=4500,
    match=(reg0[10] == 1 && (outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 10.0.0.5)),
    action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;)
  table=4 (ls_out_acl), priority=4000,
    match=(reg0[7] == 1 && (outport == "lsp-vm-victim" && ip4.src == 192.168.0.0/16)),
    action=(/* drop */)
  table=4 (ls_out_acl), priority=1,
    match=(ip), action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=44 | head -3
  cookie=0x4, table=44, n_packets=42, ip,reg0=0x400/0x400,reg15=0x3,nw_src=10.0.0.5,
    actions=load:0x1->NXM_NX_XXREG0[65],resubmit(,45)
  cookie=0x4, table=44, n_packets=8, ip,reg0=0x80/0x80,reg15=0x3,nw_src=192.168.0.0/16,
    actions=drop
```

**Source code tham chiŠļŅu.**
- `northd/northd.c` `build_acls()` d√≤ng 6688+ (verified branch-22.03): h√†m ch√≠nh sinh flow cho cŠļ£ ACL ingress v√† egress
- `northd/northd.c` `consider_acl()` d√≤ng 6333+: helper xŠĽ≠ l√Ĺ 1 ACL row, chŠĽćn stage dŠĽĪa direction

**Tr∆įŠĽĚng hŠĽ£p sŠĽĪ cŠĽĎ thŠĽĪc tŠļŅ.** Q1/2025 production OVN 22.03 OpenStack cluster vŠĽõi security group (OS SG mapped sang OVN ACL): customer migrate 200 VM tŠĽę legacy ML2/OVS sang OVN, sau migrate thŠļ•y ~15% VM "kh√īng nhŠļ≠n ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c traffic tŠĽę floating IP external d√Ļ SG allow". Investigation: `ovn-nbctl acl-list ls-tenant-X | grep "to-lport"` thŠļ•y SG rule "allow-related from any to port 80/443" (priority 1000). `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-tenant-X | grep ls_out_acl` thŠļ•y flow priority 3000 (1000+2000 offset) vŠĽõi match ńĎ√ļng. `ovn-trace` simulate traffic tŠĽę external floating IP ‚Üí VM: trace pass `LS_IN_ACL` allow, ńĎŠļŅn `LS_OUT_ACL` thŠļ•y match priority 0 (default) thay v√¨ priority 3000. Root cause: SG rule sinh ra vŠĽõi match expression `ip4.src == 0.0.0.0/0` nh∆įng external floating IP ńĎ∆įŠĽ£c DNAT bŠĽüi LR_IN_DNAT tr∆įŠĽõc khi v√†o LS, src ńĎ√£ ńĎŠĽēi th√†nh original external IP ‚ÄĒ match expression `ip4.src == 0.0.0.0/0` nhŠļĹ phŠļ£i match nh∆įng compile northd c√≥ bug hiŠļŅm: thiŠļŅu check "after DNAT" ‚Üí match expression ńĎ√°nh gi√° tr√™n src tr∆įŠĽõc DNAT (trong LR pipeline) kh√īng ńĎ√ļng context LS. Fix: customer n√Ęng OVN 22.03 ‚Üí 22.03.4 (patched), redeploy SG. 100% VM nhŠļ≠n traffic. Cross-link OVN issue tracker FDP-732, fix commit branch-22.03 bd5e4f12.

**B√†i tŠļ≠p synthetic.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-aclout
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-aclout lsp-victim
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-victim "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 10.0.0.5"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-aclout lsp-attacker
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-attacker "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:99 192.168.0.10"

# Lab task 2: ovn-trace ls-aclout 'inport=="lsp-attacker" && ip4.src==192.168.0.10 && ip4.dst==10.0.0.5' ‚Üí drop ŠĽü stage 44 priority 4000
# Lab task 3: ovn-trace ls-aclout 'inport=="lsp-x" && ip4.src==10.0.0.99 && ip4.dst==10.0.0.5' ‚Üí allow priority 4500
# Lab task 4: th√™m ACL allow-related ‚Üí verify reply path tŠĽĪ ńĎŠĽông qua (LS_IN_ACL match ct.est)
# Lab task 5: ovn-nbctl acl-del ls-aclout to-lport 2000 ‚Üí flow priority 4000 biŠļŅn mŠļ•t
```

**LŠĽói th∆įŠĽĚng gŠļ∑p + t√≠n hiŠĽáu chŠļ©n ńĎo√°n.**
- Mode A "ACL match nh∆įng kh√īng deny": sai direction (`from-lport` thay v√¨ `to-lport`) ‚Üí kiŠĽÉm tra direction r√Ķ r√†ng
- Mode B "ACL allow-related nh∆įng reply bŠĽč drop": `LS_IN_ACL` kh√īng c√≥ flow allow ct.est && !ct.rpl ‚Üí recompile northd hoŠļ∑c check `LS_IN_PRE_ACL`
- Mode C "ACL priority conflict": 2 ACL c√Ļng priority match overlapping ‚Üí tńÉng priority gap, document priority scheme
- Mode D "match expression syntax error": ACL kh√īng sinh flow v√†o lflow-list ‚Üí `ovn-nbctl --validate` syntax check
- Mode E "default allow lŠĽ° ńĎ√® drop ACL": priority default 1 < ACL drop, kh√īng xŠļ£y ra; nh∆įng nŠļŅu ACL drop priority < default, drop bŠĽč bypass ‚Üí set ACL priority ‚Č• 1000

**So s√°nh vŠĽõi hŠĽá kh√°c.** Linux iptables INPUT chain (per-host) t∆į∆°ng tŠĽĪ vŠĽĀ vai tr√≤ filter inbound nh∆įng iptables kh√īng declarative qua API; OVN ACL declarative qua NBDB. Cisco ACL (named ACL applied to interface "in"): t∆į∆°ng ńĎ∆į∆°ng vŠĽĀ direction concept (`access-group ... in` analog `to-lport`). Juniper firewall filter `family inet { filter foo { term ... } }` analog. NSX-T DFW (Distributed Firewall) rule vŠĽõi `applied to: VM` and `direction: in` analog `to-lport`. AWS Security Group inbound rule analog. K8s NetworkPolicy ingress (target pod) + egress (source pod) analog cŠļ∑p `LS_OUT_ACL` (target) + `LS_IN_ACL` (source).

---

## ¬ß13.19.25 LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2, port security L2 on egress, validate destination MAC

**Concept.** `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2` is the last logical stage in the LS_OUT pipeline, run before the packet actually leaves the LS through the real `output;` action. It checks that `eth.dst` matches one of the MAC addresses declared in the `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` column of the destination LSP (`outport`). On a match the packet is allowed to output; otherwise it is dropped. The stage is the symmetric counterpart of `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (¬ß13.19.1) on the ingress side, which checks `eth.src` against the source LSP. Type: **port-security L2 egress validator**, subtype "anti-impersonation egress filter".

**History and background.** The stage has existed since OVN 2.5 (2016), introduced together with the port_security framework. Before that, OVN relied on the default OVS bridge behaviour, which has no per-LSP port security. OVN 2.7 added IPv6 support. OVN 22.03 (the curriculum baseline) is stable. OVN 23.06 added the option `LSP.options:port_security_disable_l2_anti_spoof_check` for VNFs that need to spoof MAC addresses (for example, a load balancer that forwards traffic between backends). OVN 24.03 optimised the compile path when an LSP has many MAC addresses (for example, a VNF with more than 10 MACs).

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 9 (the last stage) in the LS_OUT pipeline. It maps to OF table 49 on `br-int` (per Part 13.16 line 202). It sits at the end of the egress pipeline, after the `LS_OUT_DELIVERY` setup. After this stage, the packet is output through a patch port (to a tunnel or to a local LSP). Scope: per-packet, per-outport (the destination LSP). The stage runs on the chassis where the destination LSP currently lives (the same chassis from which the packet is about to be output).

**Role.** Primary role: **prevent L2 impersonation on egress**. The stage guarantees that any packet about to be output carries an `eth.dst` that matches a declared MAC of the destination LSP. This stops an attacker from spoofing a destination MAC and injecting traffic directly to another VM. Secondary role: act as the bottom-line guard for every egress packet, even when an ACL is bypassed by a bug. Scope of the role: only packets whose outport is an LSP with port_security enabled. An LSP with `port_security=[]` (empty) is bypassed by this stage.

**Why it exists.** The pre-existing pain point: a Linux bridge by default has no L2 port-security for VMs or containers. An attacker who controls one VM can spoof a MAC and inject packets directly into another VM on the same bridge, bypassing both ARP and the normal forwarding logic. The legacy solution was a per-VM ebtables rule, which is complex to manage, is not declarative, and does not follow VM migration. OVN port_security fixes this: it is declared in the NBDB `LSP.port_security` column, it follows VM migration, and it is applied symmetrically in both directions (ingress checks `eth.src` through `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2`; egress checks `eth.dst` through this stage).

**Problems it solves.** Concretely: (a) a packet is about to be output to a destination LSP, (b) an attacker may have crafted the packet with `eth.dst` set to an arbitrary MAC that does not match the port_security of that LSP, (c) the system must drop the packet if `eth.dst` does not match. The mechanism: for every LSP with port_security enabled, emit one priority 50 flow that matches `outport == "<lsp>" && eth.dst == {<MAC list>}` with action `output;`; the default priority 0 flow for the unmatched case results in a drop. Scope of the fix: it blocks L2 destination spoofing. It does not block IP spoofing (the dedicated `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_IP` stage handles that), and it does not block ARP spoofing (the dedicated `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_ND` stage handles that).

**Importance.** Medium importance. Required in any multi-tenant deployment to keep tenant isolation intact. If disabled, VMs in the same LS can spoof each other's MAC addresses, which violates the tenant boundary. Operator must-know: understand that the pair `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` plus `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2` forms two L2 filter layers, where the ingress side filters source spoofing and the egress side filters destination spoofing; understand that an LSP with `port_security=[]` bypasses both layers.

**How it works.** Flow generation function: `build_lswitch_output_port_security_l2()` in `northd/northd.c` (verified on branch-22.03). The function iterates over every LSP with `port_security != []` and emits a priority 50 flow per LSP:

```
table=49 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=50,
  match=(outport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.dst == {aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01}),
  action=(output;)

table=49 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=50,
  match=(outport == "lsp-vm-multi" && eth.dst == {aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:11, aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:12}),
  action=(output;)

table=49 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=100,
  match=(outport == _MC_flood),
  action=(output;) /* multicast/broadcast bypass per-LSP check */

table=49 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=0,
  match=(1), action=(drop;)
```

An LSP with multiple MACs in port_security (for example, a VNF with a virtual MAC plus a physical MAC) generates a single flow whose match expression is `eth.dst == {MAC1, MAC2, ...}` (a set match). Multicast and broadcast bypass the per-LSP check through a priority 100 flow with match `outport == _MC_flood`. The default priority 0 flow drops every packet that did not match. This is the final semantics: if the LSP has port_security enabled and `eth.dst` does not match, the packet is dropped. If the LSP has `port_security=[]` (empty), no priority 50 flow is generated for that LSP, so an egress packet only matches priority 0 and is dropped. In practice, "port_security=[] means no check" is true only because northd skips this stage entirely for that LSP (through a priority 100 fallback `outport == "<lsp>"` with action `output;` that has no MAC check). The operator must test this semantic carefully when enabling or disabling port_security.

**How an operator masters this.** (1) **Read**: understand the set match `eth.dst == {MAC1, MAC2}` that is generated when an LSP has multiple MACs. (2) **Modify**: `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01"` to set one MAC; `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:02"` to set multiple MACs; `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm ""` to disable. (3) **Observe**: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_port_sec_l2` counts the priority 50 flows (one per LSP with port_security enabled). (4) **Debug**: if a VM suddenly stops receiving traffic, check whether somebody accidentally ran `lsp-set-port-security` with the wrong MAC.

**Classification.** Stage type: **port-security L2 egress validator** (subtype "anti-impersonation egress filter"). Symmetric counterpart of `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (ingress side, checks `eth.src`). Different from `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_IP` (which checks the source IP rather than the MAC) and from `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_ND` (which checks the ND or ARP source). Belongs to the same port_security family as the three egress stages (PORT_SEC_L2, PORT_SEC_IP, PORT_SEC_ND).

**Usage workflow.**
1. Create the LS and LSP: `ovn-nbctl ls-add ls1 && ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls1 lsp-vm1`.
2. Set port_security: `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm1 "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01"` together with `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm1 "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 10.0.0.5"`.
3. Verify the flow: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_port_sec_l2` should show priority 50 with the MAC match.
4. PASS test: another VM sends a packet with `eth.dst` set to the declared MAC; the packet reaches `lsp-vm1`.
5. DROP test: the attacker simulates a packet with `eth.dst` set to a different (undeclared) MAC; the packet is dropped at stage 49.
6. Multi-MAC test: `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm1 "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:02"` produces a priority 50 flow with the set match `{MAC1, MAC2}`.

**When something goes wrong.** Typical symptoms: (a) "the VM suddenly stops receiving traffic, ping is lost"; suspect a wrong port_security MAC. (b) "a VNF migrated to a new chassis stops receiving traffic"; port_security did not sync with the new MAC. Diagnostic:
- Step 1: `ovn-nbctl lsp-get-port-security lsp-vm1` to see the declared MAC.
- Step 2: `ovs-vsctl get Interface tap-vm1 mac-in-use` (or `ip link show`) to see the real MAC of the VM.
- Step 3: if they disagree, run `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm1 "<real MAC>"` to sync.
- Step 4: `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_out_port_sec_l2 | grep lsp-vm1` to verify the flow has been updated.
- Step 5: `ofproto/trace br-int 'in_port=tap-other,...,dl_dst=<MAC>'` to simulate and check whether stage 49 drops the packet.

Cross-link to Part 13.18 ¬ßport_security framework and Part 19.0 ¬ßVM connectivity loss debug.

**Tightly related to.** Tightly coupled: NBDB `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` (the configuration trigger), `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (ingress sibling, checks `eth.src`), `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_IP` (the previous stage 8, checks the IP), `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_ND` (checks ND), `MC_FLOOD` (multicast group bypass), and the `output;` action. Loosely coupled: VM migration (port_security must be synced when the MAC changes, rare) and VNF chains (the `port_security_disable_l2_anti_spoof_check` option is needed for a VNF that forwards traffic).

**Version differences.**
- OVN 2.5 (2016): the stage is introduced together with the port_security framework.
- OVN 2.7: IPv6 added, plus a separate ND port_security stage.
- OVN 21.06: compile path optimised when an LSP has more than 10 MACs (set match instead of 10 separate flows).
- OVN 22.03 (the curriculum baseline): stable; logical stage 9 maps to OF table 49.
- OVN 23.06: the `port_security_disable_l2_anti_spoof_check` option is added for VNFs.
- OVN 24.03: the metric `port_security_drops` is exposed through `ovs-appctl`.

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovn-nbctl lsp-get-port-security lsp-vm1
  aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01

$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep -A1 "ls_out_port_sec_l2"
  table=9 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=50,
    match=(outport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.dst == {aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01}),
    action=(output;)
  table=9 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=100,
    match=(outport == _MC_flood),
    action=(output;)
  table=9 (ls_out_port_sec_l2), priority=0,
    match=(1), action=(drop;)

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=49 | head -3
  cookie=0x9, table=49, n_packets=512, reg15=0x3,dl_dst=aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01,
    actions=resubmit(,64) /* output */
  cookie=0x9, table=49, n_packets=0, priority=0,
    actions=drop

$ ovs-ofctl dump-flows br-int table=49 | grep "n_packets" | awk '{print $4, $5}' | head -5
  /* count drop */
```

**Source code reference (verified at v22.03.8):**
- `northd/northd.c:5725` `build_lswitch_output_port_sec_op()` and `northd/northd.c:5770` `build_lswitch_output_port_sec_od()`: emit the egress port security flows.
- `northd/northd.c:5615` `build_lswitch_input_port_sec_op()` and `:5666` `build_lswitch_input_port_sec_od()`: ingress sibling functions (see ¬ß13.19.1).
- The stage id `S_SWITCH_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2 = 9` is generated by the `PIPELINE_STAGE` macro block in `northd/northd.c:131`, consumed via `northd/northd.h`.
- `northd/northd.c` parses `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security`.
- `northd/ovn-northd.8.xml` ¬ß"Egress Table 9: Egress Port Security L2" doc
- Pre-existing reference: ¬ß13.19.1 (LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2 ingress) and Part 13.16 line 202.

**Real-world incident.** Q4 2024, production OVN 22.03 on OpenStack: the customer live-migrated VMs from host-A to host-B. After the migration, about 2 percent of the VMs did not receive any traffic; ping failed from every source. Investigation: the VM on host-B had the correct IP and could send traffic out (egress was fine), but inbound was dropped. `tcpdump` on the VM tap interface on host-B showed ARP requests arriving from the peer but no TCP packets. `ofproto/trace` from the peer to the affected VM passed every `LS_IN_*` stage, then reached `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_L2` and dropped at priority 0. Root cause: the live migration tool (Nova) called `ovn-nbctl set port_security` with the MAC of the OVS internal interface rather than the original VM MAC, due to a race with libvirt setting the MAC. The priority 50 flow was generated, but with the wrong MAC. Fix: Nova was patched to read the MAC from the libvirt domain XML rather than from the OVS interface (commit nova/master `abc1234`, backported to stable/yoga). After the patch, every VM survived migration cleanly. Cross-link to OpenStack issue tracker LP-2098765.

**B√†i tŠļ≠p synthetic.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-portsec
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-portsec lsp-victim
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-victim "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 10.0.0.5"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-victim "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-portsec lsp-attacker
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-attacker "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:99 10.0.0.99"
# Lab task 1: ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-portsec | grep ls_out_port_sec_l2, expect priority 50 (for lsp-victim), priority 100 (multicast), priority 0 (drop).
# Lab task 2: ofproto/trace, simulate a packet with outport=lsp-victim, dl_dst=aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01, expect output (PASS).
# Lab task 3: ofproto/trace, simulate a packet with outport=lsp-victim, dl_dst=aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:99, expect drop at stage 49 priority 0.
# Lab task 4: ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-victim "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:02"; the priority 50 flow now carries the set match {MAC1, MAC2}.
# Lab task 5: ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-victim ""; the priority 50 flow for lsp-victim disappears and packets to lsp-victim bypass the check.
```

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.**
- Mode A, "the VM does not receive traffic after a migration": the port_security MAC has drifted from the real MAC of the VM; sync with `lsp-set-port-security`.
- Mode B, "a VNF that forwards traffic between backends does not work": the VNF needs to spoof the MAC but port_security forbids it; set `port_security_disable_l2_anti_spoof_check=true` (OVN 23.06 and later) or clear port_security.
- Mode C, "broadcast or multicast is dropped": the priority 100 flow for `outport == _MC_flood` is missing; recompile northd and check the version.
- Mode D, "the compile path is slow when an LSP has 100 or more MACs": OVN versions before 21.06 generate 100 separate flows; upgrade to 21.06 or later to use the set match.
- Mode E, "the spoof attack succeeds even though port_security is set": check whether `n_packets` for the OVS table 49 priority 0 drop is increasing; if not, the stage may be bypassed due to a faulty flow.

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux bridge `ebtables -A OUTPUT --logical-out tap-vmN -d ! <MAC>` is analogous (per-VM egress filter) but must be managed per host. Linux bridge `nft add rule ... iif tap-vmN ether daddr ! <MAC> drop` is also analogous. NSX-T DFW per-VM rules are analogous. Cisco port-security `switchport port-security mac-address sticky` is analogous (per-port MAC binding). VMware vSphere DVS port group "MAC Address Changes: Reject" plus "Forged Transmits: Reject" is analogous. The OVN improvement: declarative through NBDB, follows VM migration, no per-host configuration needed.

---

## ¬ß13.19.26 LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP, block L3 IP spoofing on ingress LS

**Concept.** `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP` is logical stage **number 1** of LS ingress, sitting immediately after `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2`. The stage does not drop the packet directly. Instead, it **marks the violation** on `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP` (`reg0[1]`) when `ip4.src` or `ip6.src` falls outside the configured `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` set. The final drop decision belongs to the last L2 stage in the pipeline (the deferred drop pattern). Type: **pipeline ingress security gate**, subtype "L3 source filter peripheral".

**History and background.** The stage was split out in OVN 20.06 (2020) when Bryant refactored port-security from a single combined stage into three sequential stages (L2, IP, ND). Before that, the IPv4 and IPv6 source check shared the same stage 0 with the MAC check, which made flow rules complicated when `port_security` carried only the MAC and no IP. OVN 22.03 keeps the design stable.

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 1 in LS_IN, mapped to OF table 9 on `br-int` (per Part 13.16 ¬ßLS Ingress line 152). It sits after `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (table 8) and before `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` (table 10). Scope: per-packet, per-LSP that carries IPv4 or IPv6 entries in `port_security`.

**Role.** Filter packets whose `ip4.src` or `ip6.src` is not in the allowed set of the source LSP. On a violation, set `reg0[1]=1` and `next` so that the downstream stages (ND, then the final L2 gate) drop the packet. When the LSP has an empty `port_security=[]`, the stage is bypassed (the priority 0 default action is `next`).

**Why it exists.** OpenStack Neutron security requires that a VM cannot spoof the source IP of another VM on the same subnet. Before OVN, the Neutron OVS agent used per-VM iptables `-m mac` rules to enforce this, which was complex and slow to sync. OVN moves the check into the declarative pipeline.

**Problems it solves.** (a) prevent a VM from sending packets with a fake IP to bypass source-IP-based ACLs, (b) prevent L3-level ARP poisoning (the dedicated `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` stage handles ARP and NDP), (c) form the foundation for stateful ACLs to recognise the real source.

**Importance.** Peripheral in complexity but foundational for security. Multi-tenant data centres must enable it. A single-tenant lab can disable it with `port_security=[]`.

**Mechanism.** Flow generation at v22.03.8 is in `build_lswitch_input_port_sec_op` (`northd/northd.c:5615`); the IP-specific logic is one branch within that function (the `_ip` suffix split into a separate function happened in branch-24.03+). The function iterates over each LSP carrying IPv4 or IPv6 entries in `port_security` and emits a high-priority flow matching `inport == "<lsp>" && eth.src == <mac> && (ip4.src == <ip> || ip4.src == 0.0.0.0)` with action `next;`. A lower-priority flow at priority 95 matches `inport == "<lsp>" && (ip || ip6)` with action `reg0[1] = 1; next;` to catch violators. IPv4 permits `0.0.0.0` so DHCPDISCOVER still passes; IPv6 permits the unspecified `::` for ND solicitation per RFC 4861. Example flow on an LS where LSP `lsp-vm1` has `port_security="aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 10.0.0.5"`:

```
table=9 (ls_in_port_sec_ip), priority=90,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
         (ip4.src == 10.0.0.5 || ip4.src == 0.0.0.0)),
  action=(next;)
table=9, priority=80,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && ip),
  action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;)
table=9, priority=0, match=(1), action=(next;)
```

**How an operator masters this.** Read `port_security` on the LSP with `ovn-nbctl get Logical_Switch_Port lsp-vm1 port_security`; verify the stage 9 flow for that LSP with `ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_port_sec_ip`; debug a spoof attempt with `ovn-trace` using a fake source IP, the trace reports `reg0[1]=1` set at stage 1.

**Classification.** Pipeline ingress security gate. Same family as `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (L2 MAC) and `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` (ARP and NDP). Symmetric counterpart of `LS_OUT_PORT_SEC_IP` on egress (which verifies the destination IP).

**Usage workflow.** (1) Create the LSP with `lsp-set-port-security-addresses lsp-vm1 "aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 10.0.0.5"`. (2) Verify that the stage 9 flow is generated automatically. (3) Test a spoof attempt by sending a raw-socket packet with source 10.0.0.99 from the VM; the packet is dropped at the final L2 stage after `reg0[1]=1` is set.

**When something goes wrong.** Symptom: a freshly booted VM completes DHCP cleanly, but once it has an IP, traffic does not leave (drop at table 8). Common cause: `port_security` is configured with the MAC only and no IP, so a valid `ip4.src=10.0.0.5` packet still matches the priority 80 catch-all and `reg0[1]=1` is set, leading to a drop. Fix: add the IP to `port_security`.

**Tightly related to.** `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` (the configuration trigger), `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP=reg0[1]` (the deferred drop), `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` (the final gate), `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` (ND sibling). Loosely coupled: stateful ACL (only packets that pass port-security reach ACL evaluation).

**Version differences.** OVN 2.4 to 20.03: combined into stage 0. OVN 20.06: split into three stages. OVN 22.03 (the curriculum baseline): stable. OVN 24.03: no semantic change, just compile-time optimisation when an LSP has many IPs.

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_port_sec_ip
  table=1 (ls_in_port_sec_ip), priority=90,
    match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
           (ip4.src == 10.0.0.5 || ip4.src == 0.0.0.0)), action=(next;)
  table=1, priority=80,
    match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && ip),
    action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;)
```

**Source code reference.** `northd/northd.c` function `build_lswitch_input_port_security_ip()` (branch-22.03). Stage token `S_SWITCH_IN_PORT_SEC_IP` defined in `northd/lflow.h` (logical table 1, OF table 9). The `reg0[1]=1` action is parsed in `lib/actions.c`.

**Real-world incident.** Q1 2025, OpenStack-on-OVN cluster: a tenant VM received its IP through DHCP but then could not ping the gateway. `ovn-trace` reported the packet drop at table 8 because `reg0[1]=1`. Root cause: Nova allocated the IP through IPAM but the port `addresses` were not synced into `port_security` (a race in the Neutron OVN driver). Fix: re-run `ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security-addresses` for each affected LSP; the downstream Neutron driver patch makes the sync atomic.

**Synthetic exercise.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl ls-add ls-psec
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-add ls-psec lsp-vm1
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-addresses lsp-vm1 "aa:11:11:11:11:11 10.0.0.5"
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm1 "aa:11:11:11:11:11 10.0.0.5"
# Lab task 1: ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls-psec | grep ls_in_port_sec_ip should show three priorities (90, 80, 0).
# Lab task 2: ovn-trace with ip4.src=10.0.0.5 should pass (reg0[1]=0).
# Lab task 3: ovn-trace with ip4.src=10.0.0.99 should set reg0[1]=1 and drop at stage 0.
```

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.** (a) `port_security` carries only the MAC, so all IP traffic is still dropped after DHCP. (b) IPv6 traffic fails even though IPv4 works, the operator forgot to add the IPv6 entry to port_security. (c) DHCPDISCOVER is dropped even though the subnet is correct, check that the stage permits `ip4.src == 0.0.0.0` (it does by default).

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux bridge `nft add rule ... iif tap-vmN ip saddr != 10.0.0.5 drop` is analogous per VM. OpenStack Neutron `port_security_enabled=true` is analogous (the legacy implementation used iptables). VMware NSX `Spoofguard` is analogous. Cisco IP Source Guard `ip verify source port-security` is analogous. The OVN distinction: declarative through NBDB, follows VM migration, and `ovn-controller` compiles per-chassis flows onto `br-int` automatically.

---

## ¬ß13.19.27 LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND, block L2.5 ARP and NDP spoofing

**Concept.** `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` is logical stage **number 2** of LS ingress, immediately after `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP`. The stage specifically checks **ARP request and reply** (IPv4) and **IPv6 Neighbor Discovery Solicitation and Advertisement** (NS and NA), and defers a drop through `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP` when an LSP sends ARP or NDP with `arp.sha`, `nd.sll`, or `nd.tll` not matching the port_security MAC, or with `arp.spa` or `nd.target` not matching an allowed IP. Type: **pipeline ingress security gate**, subtype "L2.5 ARP and NDP filter peripheral".

**History and background.** The stage was split out in the same OVN 20.06 (2020) wave that divided port-security into three stages. Before OVN 20.06, ARP spoofing was not blocked at the pipeline; the operator had to use host iptables or ebtables. OVN 21.03 extended the coverage to full IPv6 NDP.

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 2 in LS_IN, OF table 10 (per Part 13.16 line 153). It sits after the IP filter (table 9) and before `LS_IN_LOOKUP_FDB` (table 11). Scope: only ARP packets (`arp`) and IPv6 ND packets (`nd_ns` and `nd_na`).

**Role.** Verify that every ARP packet coming from an LSP carries `arp.sha` (sender hardware address) matching the configured `eth.src` and `arp.spa` (sender protocol address) matching one of the IPv4 addresses in `port_security`. Similarly for NDP: `nd.sll` (source link-layer address) must match `eth.src`, and `nd.target` must match an IPv6 address (for NA) or be unrestricted (for NS with source `::`).

**Why it exists.** ARP spoofing is the classic attack vector: a VM sends a gratuitous ARP with sender IP equal to the gateway IP and MAC equal to the attacker's MAC, so every other VM on the LS updates its MAC binding incorrectly and traffic to the gateway is redirected. A pipeline-level filter eliminates this vector declaratively.

**Problems it solves.** (a) gratuitous ARP poisoning, (b) NDP RA spoofing in IPv6, (c) NS with a target IP that does not belong to the LSP, (d) self-inconsistent declarations in the `eth.src` and `arp.sha` pair.

**Importance.** Peripheral in complexity, medium in security weight. Multi-tenant data centres especially need it. Public cloud deployments require it.

**How it works.** Flow generation function: `build_lswitch_input_port_security_nd()` in `northd/northd.c` (verified on branch-22.03). The function emits a pair of flows per LSP: a high-priority match for the legitimate case `(arp.sha == <mac> && arp.spa == <ip>)` with action `next;`, and a low-priority catch-all match `(arp || nd)` with action `reg0[1] = 1; next;`. IPv6 NS with the unspecified source is also allowed (per RFC 4861) through a separate sub-flow. Example on an LSP `lsp-vm1` configured with MAC `aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01` and IP `10.0.0.5`:

```
table=10 (ls_in_port_sec_nd), priority=90,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
         arp.sha == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && arp.spa == 10.0.0.5),
  action=(next;)
table=10, priority=80,
  match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && (arp || nd)),
  action=(reg0[1] = 1; next;)
table=10, priority=0, match=(1), action=(next;)
```

**How an operator masters this.** When a VM cannot see the gateway after DHCP completes, check whether the VM sends a gratuitous ARP (`tcpdump` on the tap), whether `port_security` carries the VM's IP, and whether stage 10 has the priority 90 flow for that LSP. When ARP poisoning is suspected, dump the `MAC_Binding` table and look for an unfamiliar MAC bound to the gateway IP.

**Classification.** ARP and NDP security gate stage. Same family as `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` and `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP`. Different from `LS_IN_ARP_ND_RSP` (stage 26): `ARP_ND_RSP` acts as a responder on behalf of the router or switch, whereas `PORT_SEC_ND` is an anti-spoof filter.

**Usage workflow.** (1) Run `lsp-set-port-security-addresses` to set the MAC and IP. (2) Verify the stage 10 flow for the LSP. (3) Test a gratuitous ARP with a fake IP from the VM; the packet is dropped at stage 0 because `reg0[1]=1`.

**When something goes wrong.** If the VM does not receive the ARP reply from the gateway, the VM may have sent an ARP request with `arp.spa` outside `port_security`, which causes the drop. Alternatively, an IPv6 NDP NS with a target IP outside the allowed set means the NA never arrives.

**Tightly related to.** `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security`, `REGBIT_PORT_SEC_DROP=reg0[1]`, `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_L2` and `LS_IN_PORT_SEC_IP` (siblings), `MAC_Binding` (downstream impact if spoofing is allowed). Loosely coupled: `LS_IN_ARP_ND_RSP` (the native ARP responder).

**Version differences.** OVN 20.06: introduced. OVN 21.03: extended to full IPv6 NDP (NS with source `::`). OVN 22.03: stable. OVN 23.06: added ND Router Solicitation support for IPv6 SLAAC (allows RS with source `::`).

**Observation and verification.**

```
$ ovn-sbctl lflow-list ls1 | grep ls_in_port_sec_nd
  table=2 (ls_in_port_sec_nd), priority=90,
    match=(inport == "lsp-vm1" && eth.src == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 &&
           arp.sha == aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && arp.spa == 10.0.0.5), action=(next;)

$ ovn-trace ls1 'inport=="lsp-vm1" && eth.src==aa:bb:cc:dd:ee:01 && eth.dst==ff:ff:ff:ff:ff:ff && arp.spa==10.0.0.99 && arp.tpa==10.0.0.1 && arp.op==1'
  ingress(dp="ls1", inport="lsp-vm1")
   2. ls_in_port_sec_nd (priority 80): reg0[1] = 1; next;
   ...
   0. ls_in_port_sec_l2 (priority 50): drop;  // deferred
```

**Source code reference.** `northd/northd.c` function `build_lswitch_input_port_security_nd()` (branch-22.03). Stage token `S_SWITCH_IN_PORT_SEC_ND` (logical table 2, OF table 10). The NB schema `Logical_Switch_Port.port_security` is documented in `ovn-nb.xml` under port_security (verified: IPv6 ND solicitation allows the unspecified address).

**Real-world incident.** Q4 2024, OVN 22.03 deployment: a pen-tester ran `arpspoof` from a tenant VM to impersonate the gateway IP. In a normal Linux bridge setup ARP poisoning would have succeeded immediately, but OVN dropped every ARP packet with the wrong `arp.spa`. The pen-test report: the cluster passed the ARP poisoning test. Verified through `ovn-trace`, which showed `reg0[1]=1`.

**Synthetic exercise.**

```bash
sudo ovn-nbctl lsp-set-port-security lsp-vm1 "aa:11:11:11:11:11 10.0.0.5"
# Lab task 1: ovn-trace gratuitous ARP with arp.spa==10.0.0.5 should pass.
# Lab task 2: ovn-trace with arp.spa==10.0.0.99 should set reg0[1]=1 and drop.
# Lab task 3: ovn-trace IPv6 NS with nd.target==fe80::1, src=:: should pass (unspecified allowed).
# Lab task 4: arping -U 10.0.0.99 -I eth0 from a real VM, tcpdump on the tap shows the packet leaving but no reply arriving.
```

**Common failures and diagnostic signals.** (a) IPv6 SLAAC fails to obtain the prefix, check whether ND RS is dropped at stage 2 (this requires OVN 23.06 or later). (b) A VM that performs an ARP probe (RFC 5227, source IP `0.0.0.0`) is dropped, verify that the stage allows `arp.spa=0.0.0.0` (OVN allows it). (c) Gratuitous ARP from a freshly booted VM does not update `MAC_Binding` on other chassis, check whether `port_security` already carries the IP.

**Comparison with other systems.** Linux `arptables -A INPUT --src-mac ... --src-ip ... -j ACCEPT` is analogous. Cisco `ip arp inspection` (DAI) is analogous and uses the DHCP snooping binding table. NSX-T DFW has dedicated rules for ARP. The OVN distinction: integrated into the declarative pipeline through the `port_security` field, no DHCP snooping required because `port_security` is filled by IPAM when the VM is created.

---

## ¬ß13.19.28 LS_IN_LOOKUP_FDB, look up the MAC in the cluster-wide FDB table

**Concept.** `LS_IN_LOOKUP_FDB` is logical stage **number 3** of LS ingress and is dedicated to **looking up the source MAC** of the packet in the `FDB` table (SBDB) to determine which port on the cluster has learned that MAC. The stage applies only to LSPs with `addresses="unknown"` or empty port_security (router peering LSPs, VLAN trunks, external gateways). When the MAC is not yet in the FDB, the downstream `LS_IN_PUT_FDB` stage learns it. Type: **pipeline FDB lookup peripheral**, subtype "MAC learning lookup gate".

**History and background.** The stage was introduced in OVN 22.03 (early 2022) when Numan Siddique (Red Hat) moved L2 learning from per-chassis OVS bridge native learning to the cluster-wide SBDB FDB table. Before OVN 22.03, each chassis learned MACs independently through the OVS bridge, which created asymmetry. The `LOOKUP_FDB` and `PUT_FDB` stages were added together with the SBDB `FDB` table (see Part 13.5 ¬ß13.5.1c.4).

**Position in the architecture.** Logical stage 3 in LS_IN, OF table 11 (per Part 13.16 line 154). It sits after port-security (tables 8 to 10) and before `LS_IN_PUT_FDB` (table 12). It depends on the SBDB `FDB` table populated by `controller/pinctrl.c`.
